<Content>Not so "Natura"; more "Comerciale"! Kudos: 1) The food was very good in the buffet area. Did not try the a la carte. New Year's Eve dinner was spectacular.2) Generally, the staff was polite and responsive. The front desk was very helpful and friendly.3) The grounds were very pleasantly groomed and maintained by the staff.4) The beach and park north of the resort was beautiful but only for walking and observing...see notes below!5) Animation staff were a blast and the dance shows were top rated.6) Our room was okay in terms of neatness and ammenities, but could have been a bit quieter and cleaner.Brickbats:1) Too many vendors on-site to 'hawk' their wares.2) Too many motorized boats and other water vehicles in the relatively small beach area. It was unsafe to swim or snorkel on the beach north of the resort due to the heavy powerboat traffic.3) The concept of a nature park was lost due to this overbearing commercialization.4) When you go to the Dominican, you expect Brugal Rum...not the cheaper Barcelo Rum served there.

<Author>jforseth07
<Content>Not the greatest place, but still had a good time! We stayed at Natura Park from Dec 4- 11/08. We paid $1950 for 2 people. All inclusive of course. We have previously been to Puerto Plata, Dominican Republic and Varadero, Cuba. We flew with Air Transat and both flights were uneventful.... this time we paid more for the extra leg room which is a MUST - definitely worth it! I would not recommend Natura Park to anyone if they asked me if they should stay there. We had very good service at the front desk, they were always attentive. The grounds are very beautiful and well taken care of. Lots of ponds, bridges, flamingos, geese, ducks and BATS at night (EWWW) The beach was amazing of course (though there was a lot more seaweed here than any of the other places we've been). The open beach to the left of the resort is very nice - secluded and nice for walking. No problems finding loungers on the beach, by the pool is a bit more difficult. The food was ok - not the greatest but we never went hungry. We mainly ate at the buffet which always had a good variety of food (pasta, stirfry, omelets, etc). The seafood restaurant was horrible - the food was undercooked and they did not even have lobster. We ended up walking out and going to the buffet instead. The steakhouse was really good, no complaints there. We did not try the Italian restaurant but heard the buffet was better. These a la carte restaurants book up fast so get your reservations in as soon as you get there. All of the bars are quite good. It seems that none of the bartenders can make the same drink though - haha - you ask for something and they will each make you a different one! The male bartender at the bar by the steakhouse made a really good strawberry daquiri (he was usually there at 6:30PM until closing). The nightly entertainment was usually very good (Michael Jackson impersonator, karaoke, dancing, etc).The rooms were something else - and not in a good way. The maids did a good job, though sometimes they take your towels at like 8 AM and you do not get fresh ones unitl 4PM..... The room appeared to be ok - a bit outdated but we are used to that from places before. Our room (# 3230 in building 12) had a major wiring problem and even though someone came to fix it twice, we had no bathroom light for 4 days. Plus we found a huge mouse in our room one night, chased it out, and looked around to find that our ceiling air conditioner had a huge nest in it..... we've never had problems like that before. The power went out quite a bit too, usually in the early evening, but did not last too long.We did the tropical storm excursion for $89 USD per person which is going out on a catamaran for the day. You leave around 8AM and return around 4PM. This was a really fun day! You get to go cruising around the ocean and go by a shipwreck just off Bavaro beach, crash through some monster waves (and got soaked!!), go snorkeling in the reef, have lunch, lots of drinks, and go to the natural pool. I would go on this one again, should we ever return to Punta Cana.We also did the monster truck tour for $90 USD per person which we really liked as well. Our tour guide Gregory made this trip a lot of fun! You drive through the countryside (with drinks of course) and stop at a typical Dominican farm where you try fresh fruits and other products, then you go to a cock fight (which I did not watch - poor things), then you stop at a Dominican school (take supplies for the kids). Then stop for lunch at the river (pretty good food). The final stop is at a Haitian voodoo village. This was disappointing as I thought we'd get to see some voodoo, no such luck. You just walk through the little hut and check out the wierd stuff inside. You leave around 7:30AM and get back around 5:30PMWe visited Manati Park when we were there ($15 USD per person.) Totally not worth it. It is like a really crappy zoo and we saw some guy hitting a parrot there who wasn't performing properly in their little entertainment gig .... I'm totally anti-animal cruelty so that was really hard to see. Don't bother visiting the mall ... there are a lot of stores but they are all quite expensive. The shuttle is free from most hotels - it drops you off and then leaves you there for like 2 hours - it will take you about 1/2 hr to walk through the mall and then you'll sit there and wait for the rest. There is a market close to Natura Park. You can find some good stuff but they really try to rip you off. The general rule is when they give you a price drop it down to half of what you are actually wiling to pay and go from there. Most of the time you end up getting a pretty good deal. You do have to walk out of the resort to get to the market and we were a bit wary at first because you have to walk through some new development and there are a lot of onlookers but every went ok - we walked there twice. The shop in the resort is also ok - but more expensive than the markets of course.I don't think I missed anything.... if you have any questions feel free to ask!  
<Date>Dec 23, 2008

<Author>lunk
<Content>Perfect for us The beach is what one goes to Punta Cana for and this place does not disappoint. The rooms are simple but always clean. We went with our 5 year old son and had a blast. People are friendly. The buffet was all we ate and it was fine. Something for everyone. None of us got sick for the first time ever in all the years we've been travelling to the Caribbean. Bring Cipro to be sure.This is a much smaller hotel system and is very well run. I didn't see it as run down. In Canada, we have much worse hotels and they're not even on a beach! We avoiding the large hotel complexes of Punta Cana in favour of this more approachable size and werre very happy we did.The diving was not so good. The most expensive I've seen and I've been diving a while. The visibility is poor due to the constant wave action and the reef looks worse than Cozumel after the hurricane. Very few healthy coral heads. Currents are strong and the fish diversity is low.

<Author>Deanna-Holger
<Content>Natura needs renovation but still charming My husband and I stayed at Natura Park from November19-26, 2008. It was our second trip there, the first was our honeymoon, 5 years ago. Once again, we loved it but the buildings are definitely getting a bit run down. For example, our room on the ground floor was very musty smelling and the mini bar was not working. The grounds are beautiful and it's fun to watch the herons and bats feeding in the ponds.  We thought the staff was great. We know a few words in Spanish and it helps a lot. Take a small dictionary along and practice, it's fun even when your pronunciation is way off. Tips are rewarded with big smiles and often even better service.The food was average and was usually cold. If you want hot fresh food, wait in the short lines for the cook to order stations: eggs, pasta, stir-fry and carving stations. There is so much variety that we always found something we enjoyed. We tried all three ala carte restaurants and thought the seafood was best. Make your reservations asap since they fill up. They were only open on certain nights, possible because the resort wasn't full.The drinks are great and if you like them strong, learn how to ask for them that way in Spanish. They will try to make anything you ask for and each bartender has different specialties. Hola to Daniel in the Bar at the stage! The games and sports are very fun and Roberto and Felix seem to work 20 hours a day to keep everyone entertained. It's a great way to meet people from all over the world so participate!The shows were sometimes contests among the guests, two nights had lip-sinced concerts that were very entertaining with good dancers and costumes, one Domincan night and one Kareoke night. We enjoyed them. Others took taxis to the casinos at night. Some nights you can take the disco tour to other resorts. I heard it was $20 and included a drink. They left between 11:00 and 12:00 and returned at around 4:00. The beach was awesome and we had no trouble finding a chair since it was the off season. You could walk for about a mile before a policeman told you to stay in his sight for security. I would have liked to walk much further. We snorkeled a bit and did find some small coral reefs with fish just to the left of the resort. We took the Bavaro Runners tour and it was great. Our guide, Eros, was awesome and spoke at least 5 languages and never stopped talking the entire day.We learned much about the island and had a really good lunch. The horseback ride was short and very poor. You have the chance to buy cigars, rum, merengue  bachata CDs, jewelry and other souvenirs. It was too windy for going into the water at the beach stop and we were swarmed with boys trying to sell us things.We also took the Saona Island tour and loved that, too but you do spend about 4 hours on a bus so it's a long day. We took snorkeling gear and used it at the island and the starfish area.Some other misc. items: There are safes and hair dryers in the rooms, You can go topless at the beach. Most guests are Canadian and European and very laid back and friendly. Many different languages spoken there. Prostitution is apparently legal.We changed dollars to pesos. 34 pesos for $1. Dollars are accepted everywhere but we got better prices when we paid in pesos.

<Author>birthdaygift
<Content>Perfect Paradise My husband and I enjoyed our relaxing stay at Natura. We were a litte nervous due to the past reviews we read. The weather was perfect. We thought the buffet could of been better . It seemed to be the same food every night. The steak restaurant was our favorite. We had a ribeye that tasted wonderful. The italian restaurant was ok. We did not experience the seafood restaurant..  The staff was very friendly, always willing to help. We did have to leave notes for housekeeping to leave more than 1 water bottle each day.  We took the Saona Island excursion. A must do! It is worth the money. We took a 1 1/2 hour bus ride to a fisherman village to get on the catamaran. The bus trip was interesting, because it took you through the towns. We got to see the culture and how the island people live and work.. The catamaran ride was fun with dancing and rum. Once we reached the island we ate lunch and swam. You could also get a massage on the beach. The palm trees were gorgeous. The palms were huge and touched the ground. The water was very clear and blue. The bottom of the ocean was a little rocky. We took our snorkeling gear, not much sea life in that part. The natural swimming pool, where we took the speed boats to was amazing. The water was like a pool and the bottom was pure white sand and very smooth. GORGEOUS! Have to see to believe. We wished we could of stayed there longer. When we got back to the fisherman village,there were island boys ages 6-12 filling water bottles up from the ocean to rinse of the tourists feet to get the sand of. My husband took some money out to pay the boy and in no time our feet were being drenched with water by many young boys all wanting money. Needless to say, we felt sorry for them and had no more money to pay the tour guide a tip.  The beach at the resort had alot of seaweed that we did not expect. Down the way to the left of the beach the grounds were very trashy. Girls also layed out with not tops on. My husband didn't mind. Ha!  The resort is a layed back kind of place. There needed to be more things to do at night. The shows got old after the first 2 nights. The gift shop was pricy on sunscreen, pack your own.  The landscaping of the resort was kept up and very beautiful. There were always gardners working.  We recommend this resort for anyone who just wants to lay back and relax! Kids would of been bored.

<Author>WebboUK
<Content>Hmmmm ... We were placed here for one night by the tour operator after our flight home was delayed for 24 hours due to a tropical storm (the resort we'd been staying at for the previous 14 nights was full so we had to move). Reception was chaos with lots of other travellers in the same boat, but the receptionists coped well and got us checked in fairly quickly. The rooms were very basic for a resort purporting to be 5*. Perhaps I'm being a little unfair - they were clean but extremely tired and dated looking, however, especially having been in a brand new modern resort for the previous 2 weeks. However, the grounds were great with loads of palm trees, birds like flamingos and herons, running around the place. The pool is too small for the number of guests. The beach area is very good with plenty of beds, shade, and inclusive watersports. The main public areas like reception, the bar and the restaurants are not air-conditioned and in the tropics this is a problem. Overall, it was fine for an emergency one-night stop, but there are far better, more modern resorts close by.

<Author>Mexico Bob
<Content>Paradise Found! Paradise Found!! For many years we had been going to an European Resort near Tulum, Mexico which was sold a few years ago and closed a couple of years ago. We especially liked that resort because of its 鈥榬ustic鈥?feel and the blend of nationalities and cultures. We鈥檝e been looking for a replacement and finally found it at Natura Park in Punta Cana.It鈥檚 been a few months since we visited and we鈥檝e been looking at some of the comments since we got back and wanted to give you our comments. We鈥檝e been to numerous all inclusive resorts all over the Caribbean, Mexico and as far away as Bora Bora.We had a fantastic vacation at Natura Park. The resort is somewhat typical in layout where there is plenty of space. The main building with reception, main restaurant, lobby bar, shops and entertainment is located someway from the beach. At the beach is another restaurant that serves lunch and becomes the seafood specialty restaurant in the evening. There is also a snack bar, beach bar, swim up pool bar and all the sports activities. The rooms are located on each side of the 鈥渃orridor鈥?between the main building and the beach in 2 and 3-story buildings. However, what鈥檚 really unique and charming are the gardens and ponds in this central corridor. The vegetation is truly tropical and there are bridges over the streams and ponds. There is fish and lots of wildlife 鈥?flamingos, geese, ducks, peacocks, etc. They stock the 鈥渇eed boxes鈥?daily with stale bread and it鈥檚 fun to get them eating out of your hands!!We found the food to be excellent and plentiful. The main restaurant is buffet style and serves breakfast, lunch and dinner. There were plenty of meat dishes, fish, vegetarian and a wellness station. And of course, plenty of deserts, fruit and my favorite 鈥?cheese. Their blue cheese was unbelievable. The beach restaurant has a varied selection for lunch and from time to time they have cookouts on the pool patio. Their paella is unbelievable!! We had one waiter, his name was Daris, and we seemed to end up on one of his tables a number of times 鈥?he was unbelievable in his level of service.Our room was nice and the air conditioning was good. The shower was fine with plenty of hot water. Again, a couple of dollars to the room maid and we never wanted for bottles of water and the refrigerator always had plenty of beer!!Now we should not forget the best part 鈥?the beach. Imagine as you look at the ocean, there are a few hotels to your right but they do not spend much time 鈥渨alking the beach鈥? To your left is nothing 鈥?just miles of beach with no buildings because it is an eco park. We love walking the beach morning and afternoon so we could walk for a couple of hours and meet just a handful of people. Yes, there is some seaweed but what can you expect when you are by the ocean. However, their team of beach guys does a great job of clearing it early in the day and they keep it that way throughout the day.All in all a great vacation. We will be back 鈥?that鈥檚 a promise!! They really are cute though.Beach: Beach was very nice, although there was some seaweed. They would clean up some seaweed and leave some. I found the staff very laid back at this resort, compared to some of the others i've been too. They didn't seem to care too much.The food at the Beach Bar was not too bad, although it was the same menu of food day after day. Always repetative. Be careful of what you put on your plate. On the last day that we left, my husband ate a date bar which was covered with ants. He didn't have his reading glasses on. The whole platter was covered with these small ants. I noticed there was a leaf from a bush that was laying on the plate, and the ants all came down from there onto these sweet bars. I had one from the next plate, which did not have one ant on it. So please be careful and watch out with your food.Buffet Restaurant: The first day at breakfast, we were not impressed. The bananas were black, the presentation of fruit was horrible. It did improve a little as the week went by, with fresh pineapple and passion fruit, our favorite. There is not a large selection of food at all at the buffet restaurant. Luckily, i love Spaghetti, so i ate that almost every day. Sometimes the blackbirds come in as everything is open, and try to snip at some of the food. One day at breakfast, I said, looks like it's going to rain. My little 4 year old niece said she felt water on her hands too. Then i looked up, and there was a blackbird sitting on a wooden shelf up above, eating watermelon while the drippings fell on our arms. At least i was glad to know it was watermelon, and not something else falling.There are no fruit decorations here like you see at some other resorts. Very plain, very little selection. But lacking here the most is the service. They are very dis-organized at the Buffet restaurant. There was always cutlery missing, no cups, no sugar, no milk. We had to get up and get it ourselves. We never complained, were nice about it, but will never return. I could see it happening once or twice, but it was every day, people were nice, but laid back, didn't care. Some of the coffee seemed like last night's coffee. It was so cold. We did tipping at Dinner time, and did get a little bit better service. One thing i noticed while sitting at the Main Bar by the restaurant.They just fast rinse the wine glasses with a j-cloth and water, no soap. I could still see the film on the glasses. They had a small dishwasher, but can't handle the amount of glasses they have.You're better off using a plastic disposable glass.Rooms: The rooms were nice, air conditioning worked well,showers were good in our room. Our relatives in the next room did have problems. Their toilet didn't work well, hardly flushed.We called the front desk 3 times on 3 different days. The kept saying, I send someone. Lucky we had our room that they can use. By the fourth attempt, they sent a service guy up at about midnight. He took a look at the toilet, and didn't improve much with it. He said the building was old, and not much more could be done. So we were almost back at square one.The maids don't do those pretty decorations with the towels there. They will just put a flower or two in your room.Near the end of our stay, we decided we were going to take the free shuttle that takes you to Palma Real Mall, about half an hour away. You'll be sorry if you go there. Everything is so expensive. Some of the simple dresses i picked up to look at were somewhere in the range of $520 and $800 U.S. Coming back was a real problem, as the van was always full of people (Bus number 41). The drive said he would be back at 3:30 to pick us up, he never returned. It cost us 20 dollars U.S. to take a taxi. We did complain to the front desk about this. He said that this bus had nothing to do with the resort. Then they should not advertise it in their brochure. Getting there is ok, every 2 hours. Be prepared to take a taxi back, and the taxi drivers don't budge, 20 dollars or nothing.Pool: Very nice, with a swim-up bar. We really loved the pool.There is a waterfall that you have to run through to get to the bar.There is also a bar above the pool area which is nice to sit at.A La Carte: We will never forget the Italian Restaurant. They went to serve us our White Wine, and my relative looked at it and said it was water. The waiter was embarrassed, as we now realized that they half fill the bottles with water, and half wine. If you notice, the bottles are never opened in front of you, they always come out already opened. He then returned with a new bottle, opened of course. The food was just ok there.The steak house restaurant was not the greatest. We found the steak a little tough there. After dinner, we asked for an Expresso or Cappucino, they said the machines were broken.The Seafood Restaurant wasn't too bad. Food was ok there.Entertainment: The dancing performers were great. I did not see a Michael Jackson show there at all. They had Mr. Natura night and Miss Natura night, where they pick someone from the audience to do different odd things and they pick a winner.If you're going to a resort for good food, this is not the place for you. I have been to the Majestic Colonial (the Best so far),as well as the Grand Flamenco and Grand Oasis. I paid over 1300 dollars Cdn. for this resort per person, not worth the money. Way overpriced for the service they provide.Sorry to be negative, but i would not recommend this resort to my friends or family, nor would i ever return there. There is muchbetter out there, and lots of other great places to choose from.

<Content>Hospitalized for three days I should know that you get what you pay for. I went to Natura Parc for what should have been a 7 day vacation from May 25 - June 1st. The total cost including airfare, accommodation, food, taxes etc. was only $890pp from Montreal. We got what we paid for, I suppose.We ended up going to the hospital to get medication for ear infections (both of us!) on the day we were supposed to leave and were hospitalized for three days and told not to fly until that weekend. The hospitalization may have colored our view of the entire stay. It seems that the hospital hospitalizes everyone who shows up for three days. It's hard not to think it's a scam - $360/night for the hospital room, $250 for each consultation with the doctor while you're there plus all the medications - $2300 for two nights and three days.On a positive note, the ground are beautiful - pink flamingos, geese, a peacock, lots of palm trees and a beautiful white sandy beach. Everything else was horrible.The rooms are small and old. Nothing works and everything is dirty. The mini bar in the room had one bottle of water, two beers and a half empty bottle of coke. Trying to convince someone to replentish it was impossible. When we arrived, I called the front desk to ask for a bottle opener (one of the few times they answered the phone). They asked me if I wanted the spa - I said no I wanted a bottle opener. After finally communicating successfully, they told me that there was no bottle opener since most of their guest brought their own! No offer to send room service with one. I later found two in the room - one on the bathroom wall (how elegant!) and one attached to the inside of the minibar.The main problem is the attitude. All of the staff seem to be unhappy, overworked and unwilling to help. We were convinced it was because the the manager at the front desk who seems to go out of his way to be difficult. My family tried to reach me several times when there was simply no answer at the front desk. The guest relations desk was a joke. The poor woman had no interest whatsoever in assisting in any way. We tipped everyone in site but it made absolutely no difference. Don't even THINK about going to the spa. I had a massage and the massage therapist actually answered the phone in the middle of the massage and continued massaging me with one hand. The manicures and pedicures are unhygenic - not to mention ugly. If you book a hair appointment, you get a wash in cold water and no blow dry!Kudos to the few staff who brightened our stay - Anthony in the pool bar (but he'd only been there a few months and didn't know how miserable to be yet) and Alberto who is the scuba instructor and was amazing. There were a few other attentive staff but with overtones of sexual harassment - definitely not a comfortable place for a woman to be without a man.I've traveled to many places and think I make a fair effort to take into account the differences in each country and had relatively low expectations due to the price but I honestly couldn't recommend this place to anyone.

<Content>Would NEVER stay at Natura Park again. My boyfriend and I returned on May 25, 2008 from a week trip to Natura Park. No kidding. I couldn't recommend it to anyone. Except maybe to someone on a limited budget seeking some sun. But then again, we've found some super deals to much nicer resorts in Cancun and the Riveria Maya for less than the cost of this trip.

<Author>SunSearcher40
<Content>Worst Place I've Ever Been! I recently returned from a week at the Blau Natura Park Eco Resort and Spa and was very disappointed to say the least. I live in Vancouver and booked my trip through Flight Centre. I booked this as a single person. I found when I got off the plane I was the only person going to the Blau Natura Park, which was interesting. It seemed that other people knew something I didn't. A lone bus came and picked me up. The guy driving didn't speak English. We went over a bumpy road to get to the hotel and when we arrived it was difficult to get any attention since I was a lone female without a male with me. I quickly found out their society is very male-dominated and I really had to try that much harder to get things like my air-conditioning fixed or get the electricity working in my room, etc. Anyway, I got a ground-level room even though I booked a top floor room because I was told the Sunquest guests only get the ground floor rooms. They don't tell you that in the brochure. Do not ask for anything at this hotel, because you won't get it. I made several requests throughout the week, ie. a bottle of cold water, towels, a doctor to come see me for a visit, etc. and none of my requests were ever fulfilled. You are on your own at this place. You just have to fend for yourself and learn to be self-sufficient and not ask for anything.FOODFirst, the food was repetitive. There were similar selections of cabbage around the buffets, or potatoes or something else. I didn't find too much variation. I have been on other trips to Puerto Vallarta with wonderful food at half the cost. They just don't put their energy into making great food here. Most everything was either shredded or cubed. You have to find your own cutlery, glasses and napkins, too if you arrive after someone's used the table before you. I got quite used to just coming in and assembling the table myself first before going and getting any food. I lost weight during this vacation.HOTEL ROOMThe hotel rooms are quite hard to find at first because everything is hidden behind palm trees and there are dark, low-lit pathways between them. My electricity went out one night and I called the front desk to get someone to come and turn it on but nobody came. I had to call 3 more times and it took about an hour before anybody arrived. I left a tip for room service every day, but found the room very inconsistent. Sometimes I had towels, sometimes I did not. Sometimes the bed was made, sometimes it was not. They also hassled me about leaving my bag in my room the day of check-out. They wanted me to pay to have it sitting in there for 4 hours, even though they could have certainly made up the room anyway. They said I was told to be out by 12 on arrival, but I am certain they did not tell me that. The Sunquest tour rep Brigitte was not there the entire week.SERVICEBe prepared, nobody speaks English here. If you go alone, you will definitely feel lonely. The tourists are 90% German or French. You hear them talking, but don't hear anybody speaking English. I finally found somebody from Newfoundland to take my picture. It was interesting because she had friends who came from Atlantic Canada, too. They all paid less than half the price I paid. I figured that was why nobody comes from B.C. but any Canadians you find there are all from Atlantic Canada and they keep to themselves. The service personnel will not answer you unless you talk to them in their language. I learned a few words in Mexico which I used here. The service staff did not seem happy. Also, they seemed kind of overworked because I saw the same people doing many different jobs around the property. Be careful not to accept glasses at the beach bars, they are not cleaned and I got food poisoning the first day I was there because of this. The man who told me changed hotels immediately, as did another two friends that he told. I stayed, however, but kept away from the water and the glasses while I was there. I tried tipping, but this didn't make any difference to the service you got while at the bars or restaurants. BEACHI liked the beach, but since I couldn't talk to anyone I found it to be quite lonely. I really envied people who could speak to their friends or mates, but I wasn't French, German or Spanish so I just read my book. Make sure you get a spot early by putting down your towel on the chair. Sometimes this doesn't work, though as I had my chair and towel used by someone once, even though it was a different colour than the hotel towels and I brought it from home. There are games during the day or dancing classes. If you want to book the water sports you have to go straight to the counter at the beach and book days in advance. Snorkelling was not good anywhere at this site. I paid the deposit of $20 cash and went out two different times, but didn't see anything substantial. I am a snorkeller and wouldn't recommend this site for snorkelling to anyone, so if you're after snorkelling, please don't waste your time.OVERALL IMPRESSIONMy overall impression was great disappointment. They call this place an eco-resort and even advertised a wellness buffet on the list of perks but I found it difficult to see how this fit the description of an eco-friendly resort. The food was not governed by wellness principles and it all seems to me a scam just to get people to come. Don't waste your money! The wildlife on the premises was nice, but that was all! The food is gross, the air conditioning is disappointing and good luck getting any towels! I would not recommend this hotel to anyone and I've been around the world. Please don't sink your money into this complex! Don't say I didn't warn you!

They start first thing in the morning houndiing you along the sidewalk and continue while you are trying to relax on the beach. It is the same at night time when the hotel takes in vendors to sell things. The vendors are very pushy and demanding which turns you off completely. The hotel should have an activity center where you can sign up for whatever event you prefer at a price that is constant. Depending on which slaeman you deal with will result in a different price.I still would go back to Natura Park as it is small enough where you don't have to stand forever in the buffet lines or at the beach bar. All the restaurants have a great atmosphere and if you never been to this part of the world, you will enjoy yourself but be ready to face the what I call salemen.

<Author>ImagineNation
<Content>Excellent! Can't wait to go back My wife and I just got back from a week at Natura Park, and I wish the week could have gone on forever!I don't understand some of the negative reviews on this site, the resort is AMAZING!The grounds are absolutely beautiful, every walk to the beach or restaurant is like a stroll through a lush Caribbean garden. The animals are all great, and yes - the some of the geese are a little cranky, but they're just noisy. We passed a lot of time watching the fish in the ponds, and the storks and flamingoes.Our room was spacious and very clean. We had a room on the top floor, and the vaulted ceiling made it seem huge. The air conditioning was perfect - we could have had the room as cool as we wanted. Throughout our stay, we always had plenty of bottled water available, and the in-room coffee was excellent.The buffet is just fine - although after a week, the same selections begin to be monotonous, but that would be true anywhere. The quality of the food was excellent. The only a la carte restaurant we tried was the seafood restaurant. It was good, nothing really special but good nonetheless. We found it was difficult to get reservations, so if you are interested in the a la carte restaurants, I would advise you to book early.The beach is probably the best thing about this resort - the beach is wide, with lots of room for swimming or sunbathing. The water is clear and the sand is soft and white. With the nature preserve right next door, it is possible to walk about 4KM return without seeing another resort. It became a morning ritual for us - nothing but the sound of the wind in the palm trees and the waves, and a few fellow walkers.The 'nightlife' is okay, but it doesn't really seem to be the focus of this resort. This was perfect for us, because we were looking for more of a relaxing and peaceful vacation. The shows each night were pretty entertaining, but the fact that this isn't a 'party' resort meant that there weren't a lot of rowdy college students around. If that's what you're looking for, this probably isn't the place for you.There are lots of available activities on the beach - we used the masks and snorkels, the pedal-boats, and the kayaks, and had a great time. We were going to use the catamaran as well, but ran out of time. There didn't seem to be a problem getting time with the equipment, except on the weekend when the resort was very busy with locals.We did two excursions, both of which I highly recommend. The Caribbean Festival includes swimming with sharks, and holding stingrays (the barbs removed, of course), snorkeling along a coral reef with lots of fish, and a Caribbean-themed dance act and party on the boat. It's a half day for U$55pp. The Monster Truck Safari is a full day for U$95pp, and worth every penny. The safari takes you into the beautiful rolling hills around Higuey, where you meet many locals, see working farms, sugarcane plantations, and have lunch by a beautiful river. Our guide (Gregory) was AWESOME! He made the day so much fun, and is very knowledgeable about the history.The best part of our stay at Natura Park was the staff. With only VERY few exceptions, 99% of the staff here are very friendly, helpful, and they all seem like they LOVE their jobs. They're happy and playful, and love joking around with guests. We did our best to speak with them in the little bit of Spanish we know, but they were all very able to help us in English as well.There's only one small thing that I would point out as a concern: the childrens' playground was overrun with bees or wasps. We didn't have a child with us, but if we had, it wouldn't have been possible for them to play there. Hopefully they can find out what is attracting them and get rid of them.I will be recommending this resort to all of my friends, and I wholeheartedly recommend it to anyone looking for a wonderful, peaceful vacation.

Eating too much is a big one, how often does one have the opportunity to stuff themselves full of a wide variety of different food as many times a day as they want and drink their guts out at the same time, no wonder they get sick. Pace yourself your body is not used to many of these habits. Not washing there hands, using the tap water for brushing teeth. I always carry alcohol hand wash for after using the washrooms or after touching areas that many people are around etc.Use the bottled water for your teeth. Stay away from mayo based salad dressings and cold meats. Keep an open mind and just enjoy the weather after all you are in a country where the sun will bake you inside of a half hour.Use sun screen often. I reccomend spf 30+ if you have fair skin. Drink lots of water. Ask for extra in you room.Drink the two they give you regardless of how much else you drink, every day. Heat exhaustion and dehydration are another big cause of illness,they often present as poisoning Enjoy the weather, enjoy the people around you.Open your mind and your heart will follow.I welcome your email if you have any questions.

Our kid鈥檚 bathroom seemed to draw in foul cigarette smoke from their neighbor鈥檚 suite in just this way. It was bad enough that the louvered bathroom and toilet doors provided no privacy in our own suite.Members of our group participated, when they were able, in activities including swimming with dolphins, kayaking, golfing, snorkeling and a shopping trip to Higuay. I personally enjoyed golfing three times which was booked through the Guest Services desk in the lobby. We chose the cheapest package, at the Catalonia Caribe Golf Club, which cost 100 USD (3400 Pesos) and included hotel transfers, range balls, 18 hole green fee and cart. The course was decent, well maintained and not far away. Other golf packages could be had for as much as 370 USD at more auspicious courses. We also enjoyed the one hour snorkel trip (yes, the same as noted above, but later in the week) for about 10-15 USD per person. The people who travelled one hour by bus to Higuay said they were creeped out, ending up in a slum area, accosted by intimidating locals trying to sell their wares (or rob them). Higuay was not recommended.The big problem that we faced was that of gastroenteritis. Fourteen of our group of sixteen experienced diarrhea, vomiting, nausea, headache and general achiness. A few people had relatively mild symptoms, while most of the others, including my wife and son, were quite sick and unable to leave their rooms anywhere from one day to three days; missing dinners, activities and generally wasting hard-earned vacation dollars. Once able to escape the toilet, they still felt ill with a loss of appetite, lethargy, etc. It just sucks to feel that way anywhere, but especially on vacation, and we are really annoyed! We all went through a lot of Immodium, which provided minimal relief. The onset of this sickness occurred at various times during our stay. I, myself, succumbed to this souvenir of Natura Park shortly after arriving home this evening and I am writing this account in between painful cramps and trips to the toilet where I have been expelling what feels to me like battery acid. I should be sleeping in preparation for a busy return to work, but I cannot sleep. I have always purchased Immodium before our travels, but this is the first time I have ever had to use it. Thank goodness I still have some left over.After careful introspection, we could not conclude the origin of this illness. I think it may possibly be related to poor training and hygiene amongst the food handlers. Therefore, I cannot warn the reader to stay away from the ice or the lettuce or the juice or whatever, but perhaps the best advice would be to stay away from this resort and/or from Punta Cana. Most of my group are seasoned travelers with experience in places like Cuba and Mexico. We are not reckless or na茂ve, but we have never had to deal with anything like this and I doubt that any of us will go back to Punta Cana. One of our party spoke with a manager on our last day to express her concerns. The manager, who was very polite and understanding, said he also experiences gastrointestinal upset after returning from occasional trips to Spain and he considers this to be a normal and natural event. I fear this attitude may be endemic at the Natura Park and such denial will ensure this problem will never go away until perhaps the tourists themselves go away.

<Content>We had a wonderful time. My husband and I stayed at Natura Park from 3/7 to 3/12. We were very nervous after reading all the negative reviews on trip advisor and started second guessing our choice. However, we had an absolute wonderful time. We had absolutely no problems checking in and our room was ready as soon as we got there. It was clean and everything was in working order. The shower had some cracked tiles but again that didn't matter to us as long as the shower worked and the water was warm. The grounds were absolutely beautiful. We have heard complaints about the seaweed and our response to this is, yes, there is alot of seaweed that washes up on shore BUT their are workers working their butts off going back and forth with wheel barrows cleaning it up and why people comment on this when it's completely out of the hotels control and all about nature is beyond me. As far as the food is concerned, it was good, we never had a problem finding something to eat. Again, when you mass produce food like this everyday it will sometimes be not hot enough, or the same as the day before but that comes with the territory at an all inclusive. We only ate at the ala carte steak restaurant and it was good. The service was great. We never had to look for any of our silverware, like we read on this site, it was always on the table. We found that everyone that worked at the hotel were very friendly and also found that if you try speaking a little spanish (thank you, please) that they were very receptive. We were advised to tip a dollar or two while we were there and at first I was against this being at an all inclusive but we ended up doing it and I was glad that we did. They are very grateful! The bartenders work very hard and long hours, we were constant visitors to the bar by the pool and Iris was VERY good to my husband whenever he came to get drinks, tipping went along way!!Now for the chair situation. We were always up and ready for the pool or beach by 7:30 and we never had a problem finding chairs. The pool wasn't an issue and as far as the beach is concerned, people do save chairs and they are usually the ones with the huts that are saved. It's frustrating but b/c we were always down there so early it wasn't ever a problem. If you like to sleep in and plan to get to the beach and pool at 11am, be prepared to have a hard time getting chairs.The shows were good but to be honest, we were only able to stay up for two of them b/c we were so tired and in bed by 10:00 each night. The only suggestion I have for the hotel is to change the games at the pool so your not doing the same ones ever day and to play some newer music as well.We met great people the whole time we were there and such a relaxing time. We would go back again and would also reccommend it to others. But, if you aren't laid back and are extremely picky and want everything to be perfect then this isn't the place for you. Just remember, you are on an island and everything is on a relaxed slower pace.Have a great time when you visit!!

<Author>travLR123
<Content>Relaxing Vacation in the Sun We are a couple in our mid 30's and we stayed at Natura Park in February 2008. If you are expecting to be waited on hand and foot, then this is not the place for you, but if you are just looking for a place to chill out and relax, you'll have a great time. The resort is beautiful. The beach is large, and although it was crowded we never had trouble finding beach chairs when we wanted them. I only went in the pool once as it was a bit cold. The ocean was nice though!We were initially assigned a room with double beds but we asked to be switched to a room with a king bed and they switched us a day later. Our maid did a great job keeping our room clean and she left lots of towels and facecloths. There are quite a few TV channels, including many English language ones. Our room had a small balcony. Many of the items in the minibar come at a steep price; we avoided those but when we checked out they still tried to charge us for something we didn't drink. The desk clerk resolved the problem quickly though.The buffet is fine - there is lots of variety and although the buffet closes for a couple hours between meals, there are snacks available all day at the beach. The buffet offers omlettes and smoothies at breakfast, custom pasta dishes at lunch, and lots of salads and healthy choices. There are several bars, with good drinks, both alcoholic and nonalcoholic. We sometimes had to wait a few minutes for drinks at the bar but generally the servers were friendly and we noticed that they seemed to work very long hours. We didn't enjoy the food at the specialty restaurants (we thought the buffet was better), although they are worth it for the ambiance.The evening entertainment is average, but the performers are enthusiastic and most of the people seemed to enjoy it. We took one trip off the resort (the half day Outback Safari) but we didn't enjoy it as much as we thought we would. A lot of the time was taken up driving around to other resorts picking up the other passengers; the actual tour portion of the day was quite short. I had a massage at the resort's spa but I wouldn't recommend it.We went to a travel clinic before our trip and got the anti-malarial medication and immunizations we needed. We avoided tap water and we had no health problems at all. There were a few mosquitos; we used repellant in the evening and weren't bothered by them.All in all, we had a great week. We didn't pay a lot for our vacation and we think we got good value. If you are looking to be pampered you should probably go elsewhere but if you just want to put your feet up on a beach for a few days, this resort is great.

<Author>Icebabe2002
<Content>Beautiful looking, but hit or miss on everything else Just arrived back from a Sunquest vacation to the Blau Natura Park. It is hard to give an overall impression of the hotel as some things were great, while others poor. The hotel is a short 20 minute drive from the airport (nice looking airport, but the staff will try to extort as much money from you as they can...). It really is in the middle of nowhere, and the area is not pleasant smelling once you get off the resort property.The property itself is quite nice, more natural looking than most - with the exception of the fish ponds/lagoons that are very clearly artificial. It is fun to see and feed the fish and birds that are all over the place. The buildings incorporate a lot of natural materials, which give it a more rustic feel. The beach is a decent size, but there is a lot of seaweed. This is mainly due to the strong winds (which actually help keep you comfortable during the day).The rooms were a disappointment. Everything in them smells musty, and we had little ants of some kind in the bathroom and on the desk. Thankfully, they didn't get into our stuff. The beds were harder than any futon I've ever slept on, and I had a sore neck all week as a result. The electricity is definitely an issue - some of the lights didn't work, and a surge blew out my battery charger. We did have hot water and the A/C worked well, so we were lucky compared to some. Don't travel with anyone you might be shy around, as the bathroom doors are made of slotted wood, and only slide back and forth. Note that noise carries pretty easily, especially near the theatre.The food was hit or miss. Generally, when the meat was cooked properly, it was quite flavourful. The pasta was generally okay. There were issues with keeping food hot though, and both me and my friend ended up with intestinal problems (and when they say don't drink the water from the taps, this includes brushing your teeth!). The a la carte restaurants weren't anything special. Service varied wildly depending on who you had, although the people at the bars were quite nice. Considering the variety of countries that they draw visitors from, I was impressed that most staff could converse in English, French, Spanish or German. The entertainment staff tried, but some of the shows were a litlle slow. Excellent dancers though.The prices at the hotel store were decent (good selection if you forgot anything), but you could get better if you haggled well with the merchants that came on site a few times a week. Don't accept their first or second offers though! They do get a bit annoying though as every one of them wants you to stop and look at their stuff. None of it is really original, as you can get the same items elsewhere on the island if you go into town or on a tour. Do take a tour though, as it will give you a better idea of the island outside of the hotel.  I am glad I went, but I wouldn't go back to this hotel again.

When you first get there they walk the beach and ask you if you want to do any activities like horseback riding.. dune buggies.. snorkling etc. But they don't bug you if you don't want to do it just say no... then they go to the next person they don't hassle you, they just want you to have a good time there and take advantage of everything that they have to offer.We did the dune buggy's so much fun!! we loved it. Some friends of ours did the out back and they loved that..We did the snorkling where they take you out in a boat just out front for an hour and snorkle awesome!! take bananas or bread with you..it was $15 u.s each.My daughter and 3 of her friends went parasailing they loved it!! My sister in law and I were able to go in the boat so that we could take pictures, that was such an experience.The one thing that we could never get used to is the smoking..on the entertainment nights people smoked all around you and when your not used to it you notice it..The 3 ala Carts we went to we loved the Italian the food was so tasty and cooked perfectly.The steak was awesome!! We mostly had the Rib eye but the second week my sister in law had the tenderloin with mushrooms and it was better their soups are so hot and delious sooo good.We didn't care so much for the seafood one we found that the seafood had a weird taste to it (and Iam not picky) We didn't complain tho they noticed that I didn't eat much and asked if I would like something else they were so willing to please..we just went to the buffet after and had something else.The bufffet is only open till 10 pm so when we got there late when we first arrived we were so hungry the one thing that we thought that the company should have is a small buffet for people when they first get there from their plane ride because you are starving and nothing was open..They do have a later place where they serve fries and hamburgers and hotdogs starting at 12 am to 5 am but when we were looking for something at 10;30 their was nothing.. We found that you really had to look for beach chairs it's a big beach tho and sometimes you had to walk a little further to find one and sometimes you had to sit in the sand because their was none. We noticed people were taking peoples towels off and taking the chairs anyways (which I don't agree with) we had to get up very early just to save the seats and some people were there at 6am to get seats and then someone comes along at noon and just takes the towel off the seats and steals it. NOT RIGHTThe animation team was awesome!! they really kept you involved in all the activities Dancing ....shows...water arobics...volleyball..soccer.. archary... if you wanted to do it fine and if you didn't want to do it nobody forced you to partake. Wilson.. Johnny be good..luis... awesome people!! ask for them they always have a smile on their faces and are happy to help you with any activities that you may want to do..They do have a gift shop there but if you want to walk down the beach they do have a small village and they have a row of gift shops that you can go to and wheel and deal with them ( don't take the first price that they offer most times you can cut the price in half) The rooms were ok we asked for a King size bed but never got it instead we got 2 double beds but it was fine no problems it was clean and the maid did a great job we left a tip everyday on the bed and a small gift (they like perfume..lipstick..hair clips...pens..toothbrushes.. things like that) since they are so poor they really do appreciate those things. We left all our hair products and creams and perfumes etc to some people that could really use it that lived there..you would have thought that they won the lottery they really do appreciate it.We had a awesome vacation and hope to go back soon..It's a wonderful resort and I wouild recommend it to all.

Pool chairs were hard to come by, unless you were up early and down to the beach or pool to claim them with your towels, but that really was no hardship. I would recommend it to anyone wanting to see the country side. <Author>dingdingeyes
<Content>Great Resort and a few but... My boyfriend and I went to Natura Park Resort with Signature Vacation from Jan 21 to Feb 4. Overall it was a good resort with a few problems:ArrivalWhen you get to the airport lobby, remember to go to the booth on the right left of the lobby to see which bus # you are getting on. We were a little confused at the beginning because signature vacation didn't have a rep with a sign at the lobby. But don't worry, they won't take off without you. Check inWe didn't get a lock for the security box when we checked in, but got it without a problem the next morning. When we arrived it was around 10:30pm, and the buffet was already closed at that time. There was a snack bar opened from 12am midnight to 5am. So if you are arriving late as well, remember to bring some snacks~RoomWe got a room with two double beds on the ground floor. When we talked to another two couples also from our flight, they said they got rooms with two double beds too. One of them requested for a room with king size bed and they got a room that was quite close to the disco bar, so it's quite noisy at night. Other than the double beds, our room was great! Perfectly fine air con, very clean room with no bed bugs, no water leaking from above... Our room is not facing the beach but it's very close to the beach and the flamingo pond~ The room is really big (bigger than the other all-inclusive hotels that we have been too). There was no alarm clock, so really remember to bring a clock or a watch (you can also check the time on channel 40 on the TV~) There was a hair dryer in the bathroom, it's very weak but it worked fine (keep in mind it's a eco hotel~) The water pressure for the shower was surprisingly good! Some people here mentioned about the wooden doors for the toilet and the bathroom. It's not very sound prove, but we just turned up the TV volume and it's fine =)The maids did a good job cleaning the room. We brought little gifts to them, like toys, crayons, etc. They liked to use flowers to decorate instead of making towel animals. The flowers did attract some tiny little ants, I usually just moved the flowers away from the bed and it's fine~There was a mini bar fridge in the room, but not everything in there was included. You get 2 big bottles of water (outside the fridge) and 2 local beer and 2 pop (inside the fridge) every day. Other things like import beer, chocolate bar and chips cost money. Sometimes they might leave you a bill even you didn't get anything from it, but you just have to tell the front desk that you didn't take anything and they will cancel the bill. We live on the ground floor, so we were quite worry about security after reading some reviews that some people's room got robbed. We always locked the chain on the balcony door, put all valuables in the lock box and locked our suitcase whenever we left the room. Nothing was stolen~GroundsThis hotel really has the most beautiful ground! The mangroves and the ponds were very nice. The flamingos, ducks, geese and other birds made our stay a lot more interesting~ It's fun to see the birds do different things every time we saw them~ I do wish the hotel have more chairs around the ponds, so I can sit there all day to look at the birds~ There are also some wooden boxes beside the ponds that had some left over bread for guest to feed the birds and fish. PoolThe water of the pool was really quite cold. BeachThe beach was really nice! The sand was soft and there was no sand flea. There were quite a bit of sea weed as mentioned in other reviews as well. I didn't mind them when they were on the beach, but they felt a bit gross when they were around me in the water. They didn't have enough beach chair for every guest. We usually left two towels on two chairs before we went for breakfast. If you walk to the left of the beach, you can find a long strip of beach that doesn't have much seaweed and has no hotels on it. There are some places around there that's good for snorkeling. We tried to keep walking to see if we will get to Bavaro beach, but it got to a point that there weren't any foreigner along the road and it looks like it's still a long way, so we just headed back.FoodThe food in the buffet was... inconsistence. Some days it could be really good and some days it could be really bad... Breakfast is always good at the omelet station. They also have packaged yogurt there~ Lunch - we usually spent our lunch around the beach and went to the buffet once. The lunch buffet near the beach was good. They got a soft ice-cream station there. There was a snack bar near the beach that served burgers, hot dogs and fries. Once in a while, they would have chefs that cooked in front of the pool. They had this seafood and curry spice rice or noodles there that it's the best thing I ever had! I'm still missing it now... The lunch buffet at the lobby buffet was not that good...Dinner - buffet was again, inconsistence, most the time it's ok though. Their dessert is very very good! The a-la-carte was kinda funny...Some food (esp. appetizer) were just not quite what you expected. The steaks at the steakhouse were good~ The chicken and the beef at the Italian restaurant were good too. We didn't go to the seafood restaurant. EntertainmentSome reviews said the entertainment was poor, but I think they were great! Both at the pool area and the disco bar were very entertaining. They usually have games played with the guests on most nights. The also have couple shows - the stars night and the Michael Jackson night were awesome! We stayed for 2 weeks and they didn't have identical shows everyday for both weeks. ServiceOverall is ok... Some people were really good, like Pedro at the buffet! But they were a bit understaffed... especially at the bar area. You really have to tip someone to get a drink or expect to wait for at least 20 min. There were some people from the hotel that sells tours. They were fun to see and talk to in the first couple days, but when you still haven't buy any tour from them they could became quite pushy... We went on the boogie tour from them and it was great~ShuttleThere was a free shuttle bus from the hotel to a shopping mall called Palm Real. The mall is not quite worth going to because it's really small and sells really expensive things, but it's right next to Palm Real hotel in Bavaro~ We didn't have enough time or we would for sure go walk around that area. There was also a free shuttle bus to go to the manati park in Bavaro. Outside the hotelThere were some stores outside the hotel (about 5-10 min walk) that sells souvenirs. There was also a convenient store there that sells things that were a little bit cheaper than the gift store in the hotel. Consider this was the cheapest resort we found in Punta Cana, I think it's a great resort! The ground was definitely worth staying~

<Author>jdsjas
<Content>Over rated My husband and I have travelled quite extensively in the Caribbean. This is the first time we would say that the resort was definately not worthy of the 4 star rating. The grounds are nice and kept tidy. The hotel itself is tired. We were supposed to have a king bed and ended up with 2 3/4 beds. The beach could be very nice but has a lot of seaweed and it seems to be the only hotel along that strip that doesn't clean it up. They seem understaffed and understocked. Towels are often not available and if you need a spoon, you'll likely be going on a treasure hunt. Seats on the beach are also difficult to find. If you'd like wine with your dinner, no problem. If you want a beer, you may have to ask about 3 different servers. You still may not get one, and they don't seem overly concerned. The food is ok, although I think it could be kept warmer. The steak house restaurant is very good. We managed to eat there twice. This restaurant is also off of the beaten track of Punta Cana. Outside the main gates is filthy and the local market is nothing short of harassment. My advice - go somewhere else!

<Author>waterlogged23
<Content>Great Value for the Money My husband and I stayed at Natura Park Resort from January 21 - 28, 2008. We were somewhat skeptical before we went after reading some of the reviews, but were pleasantly surprised at the quality of the resort and service once we arrived. We had a smooth check-in and were shown to our room which was right at the beach, pool and upper bar. Great location!The food was good. You will never go hungry. Everyday at lunch aside from the buffets and snack bar they also had an outdoor grill going by the pool and made some delicious stir fry dishes. We tried two of the specialty restaurants. The food was OK, but actually you have more choices with the buffet. Our room was wonderful. Extremely clean - flowers on the bed and in the bathroom everyday. Floors mopped and clean towels everyday. Absolutely no complaints with the room or the housekeeping staff.Drinks at the bar seemed to be watered down or were extremely weak. However, the staff did not seem to have a problem with giving doubles when asked. There are two bars right on the beach, so you don't have to go far for a drink. The beaches are beautiful. The water was warm and clean. The sand is more like powder than sand. The skies were clear blue, with a nice breeze to help cool you off. The grounds are extremely clean and beautiful. The bridges over the mini water areas, along with the flamingos, ducks, geese, herons and fish make it even more special. The plants/flowers were incredible. HOT TIP: Regarding the beach chair situation. We got skunked the first day in getting a beach chair. We soon figured out a way to have a perfectly placed beach chair everyday thereafter. We would go down to the beach at night around 10:00pm and pick out two good chairs, place them under a thatch hut, (right by the bar!) and then wrap our towels around the top of the chair. Don't do this with the resort towels because if they get taken you will have to pay $10.00 each. So take a couple of your own old towels and you should be set. It is unfortunate that you have to resort to this, but if you really want a chair you either have to get up before 0600 or try our trick and have a sleep in!ONLY COMPLAINT: The smokers! Coming from beautiful British Columbia, Canada, we are not used to smokers - especially smokers at meal time. There was suppose to be no smoking allowed in the restaurants, but they don't seem to enforce that rule, which was rather disappointing. However, a small complaint when everything else was so nice, so we tried not to dwell on the smokers and just moved if we had too many of them around us.BEST ACTIVITY: Find Johnny Be Good (black pants, red polo shirt and big smile) and book a sunset horseback ride. The best $40.00 value you will ever have. Galloping along sandy beaches as the sun sets was the best fun ever! Also the Catalina Island Snorkelling Trip is great. A long day 0700 - 1900, but well worth it. The crew were so much fun and the waters are beautiful.BOTTOM LINE: For the price you get a clean resort, good food, and beautiful surroundings. The staff were always friendly and liked to help us with our spanish when we asked. We will definitely go back to this resort.  
<Date>Feb 2, 2008

<Author>saskabush08
<Content>Fabulous time at Natura Park! My husband and I just returned from Natura Park for our second honeymoon and we had a great time. We had never travelled to an all-inclusive resort before so we have nothing to compare it to, but we were quite satisfied with our experience. I was a bit wary after reading many of the reviews on this site, however the positives definitely outweighed the negatives. We booked through a CAA agent with Sunquest and paid around $1700 per person.Check-in: Quick, staff were helpful. We didn't get a safe key at first since they had run out (hotel was over-booked), but we got one the next day no problem, and they offered to keep our passports overnight in the hotel safe if we wanted to. Rooms: Pretty good, we were in the first building next to the buffet and bars, so at night it was a bit noisy, but we're sound sleepers so it didn't bother us. Since the hotel was so busy, we didn't bother trying to change rooms. We had a king-sized bed and the air conditioning worked well. There were a few things in need of minor repairs (shower head, toilet paper holder), but you spend so much time outside, who cares???? Maid was good-we tipped her $1 US a few times and left small gifts. Food: Overall very good. There was good variety at the buffet for every meal, if you couldn't find something you liked then you must be pretty picky! The fruit and wellness buffet were good, as was the beach BBQ for lunch, the pasta bar, omelette bar, and the mexican restaurant (have the tenderloin!!!!). Desserts were good too! We never went hungry. I got a bit sick after the seafood restaurant, but I was eating everything (fresh salads, cut fruits, etc) so I wasn't surprised really. The resort uses filtered water for washing food and making ice. Go early for the buffets to get the freshest/hotest food. The restaurants are all open-air, so there is always going to be the challenge of keeping food hot/cold and fresh for several hours. Grounds: Beautiful! Very well taken care of. Lots of critters to feed and watch (birds, fish, turtles, etc), lovely trees and flowers. Pool/beach: Beach was great, go early to get a chair (before 8 am when it's busy and the weather is nice). Didn't spend much time at the pool since the beach was so great. There is some seaweed, but it gets raked up everyday. You can walk for probably 1.5 hours to the left before you reach the next resort, good swimming and snorkling spots along the way. Entertainment/Activities: We really enjoyed the evening shows, and the daily activities were pretty good too-hard to get people together for a VB or soccer game since most are older or just there to bake :)Service-Very good. We never had to wait for a table, and they were very efficient at the a la carte restaurants.The resort was very busy, but we never had trouble getting drinks or food. Don't expect to be waited on hand and foot-and remember the staff work long hours and get paid very little! Many travel over 2 hours to work every day. They do their best and are always smiling!We went on the Caribean Festival and 8x8 monster truck safari tours and had a great time on both-make sure you leave the resort for your shopping! There are vendors that come in a couple times a week with stuff, but they are very overpriced and aggresive. Watch out for fake amber and larimar! Be early for the buses that pick you up for tours since they'll leave without you if you're not there ;)If you are a very picky eater, used to being waited on hand and foot, and anything going wrong will spoil your vacation, you should just stay home because the rest of us don't want to hear your whining! Remember, you're there to have fun, relax, and enjoy the sunshine-which we had no trouble doing at Natura Park!

<Author>Jose-Anita
<Content>Great value We are an adult couple who takes at least two vacations a year in all inclusive hotels in the Caribbean. We have been to more than 10 different hotels in the last few years; therefore we can compare them with ease.My wife and I spent a week at the Natura Park Hotel between January 12 and 19. It is our third visit to this Hotel. We had been there the year it opened (1997) and again in 2002 . Of all three visits, in our opinion this was the best. Food quality has improved at the main buffet, there is diet food available for those who need it, although the hotel was full we never had to wait to eat at the main buffet, the food at the Italian restaurant was excellent, the quality of alcoholic beverages and wine is above average to other hotels of the same price range in the Punta Cana Area (Baileys at the main bar, bottled Spanish and Italian wines with all meals). General maintenance of the hotel is good, pool is clean, room was always made up early in the morning, never a towel missing in the bathroom, free safe in the room, beautiful but simple and natural setting all around.The characteristics we like best about Natura Park are:Marvelous gardensVery low buildings well blended with natureBeautiful quiet beach with lots of shade The atmosphere at the main bar and lobby is very relaxed.Because it is not to large a hotel, everything is close by.Low noise almost everywhereNo pressure to participate in activitiesVery restful vacationSuperb leisurely walks on the beach to the left of the hotel because there is a very long stretch of virgin beach without any other hotel for at lest 2 to 3 km.Located far away from the crowded stretch of beach near Cortecito which starts at the Barcelo hotels complex and ends at Breezes with more than thirty hotels one besides the other.Comparing this hotel to several others within the same price range, we consider the Natura Park one of best values for your money in the Punta Cana Area and we highly recommend it to people who are looking for a relaxed and restful vacation at a very reasonable price.

<Author>McBeans
<Content>Sunny vacation near a nature reserve We stayed at the Blau Natura Park from Dec. 30/07 to Jan. 6/08. We are a professional couple in our early thirties. I will break up the review into sections to help.THE BEACH - Natura Park is on a section of the beach that has nice white sand. The water is clear but does have quite a bit of seaweed in it that also washed onto shore. There are many boats in the vicinity that sometimes make noise and odours. However, walking north there is an expansive nature reserve and the beach here is beautiful and water is mostly clear. There is also good snorkeling at this part of the beach. Downside is that there are obviously no beach chairs off the resort.THE FOOD - The food was good. Many options at the buffet. Sufficient choices for vegetarians and health-conscience. We did not get sick. The buffet is better than the a la carte restaurants. The beach buffet is better than the main restaurant for lunch. All night burgers/hot dogs/fries is also available.THE RESORT - Very nice looking and well kept. Many tropical birds throughout in man-made lagoons. The room was sufficiently clean and did not smell. The beds were also fine and were clean. Everything is in short walking distances. They were at capacity the week we went and they were not prepared. They frequently ran out of dishes at the buffet, food items, towels and restaurant reservations. The beach was also packed and they did not have enough chairs for about half of the week.SERVICE - About 75% of the service staff is either rude or indifferent. Of course there were exceptions. Although I do not expect the hotel staff to speak english, I was surprised at how little English was understood. Basic words like cup, ice, towel, toilet paper, shower and lime were not understood. I just made an effort to learn the spanish words, but it was a challenge to communicate. We had a problem with the mini-bar where somebody was taking items and we were getting charged. But we complained to our tour rep and it got fixed. We also had an issue where we were not told that it would cost $3 everytime we picked up the phone, even with a phone card or collect calls. We challenged this and the fees were cut in half.OTHER - I did not use the pool myself but it looked clean, was large and had a bar. Tennis courts were available and were in good shape. Entertainment was on the cheesy side. Very little imported alcohol and no drinks that require a blender to make. We did a Outback excursion that costs about $100 a person. It was okay, but I would not recommend it unless you really want to see some villages, the mountains and areas outside the resort. The coffee and cocoa plantation as well as the authentic Dominican restaurant did not look genuine, rather they seemed assembled for the tourists.Overall, I would return to the Blau Natura Park but I would not go at peak seasons.

<Content>Great overall resort We booked this air/hotel through Apple Vacations.Flight: USA 3000 from BWI to La Romana then to Punta Cana went smoothly except they did not have enough food for everyone on the plane. Poor customer service.We wizzed through the airport to the busses due to the normal Apple efficiency. Bus to the hotel took about 1/2 hour with the stops at the other hotels to drop off others.This resort is a well maintained with mature vegetation insteed of the newer resorts where the planting look like the were stuck in the ground yesterday. My wife would have been happy to watch the resort's birds catch fish in the lagoons all day.We walked to the beach, turned left (north) and walked for an hour on a road that paralelled the beach for 1 1/2 hours to the next populated area. During the walk we took a path inland and saw coconut harvesting areas. Great smells of fermenting cocconuts. Along the walk back along the beach the sand gives way to coral with tidal pools. Great for seeing crabs, star fish etc. Wear good footwear as the coral will slice your feet.Food: The best time to eat is when the buffet first opens for the respective meal. The food is hotter and the lines for the specialty prep areas are short or non existant. Remember to wash your hands often as you greatly decrease your chances of either end problems. We had no ill effects on theis trip.When we first got to the room it was dark and flipping the switches did not turn on the lights. With some help from passers by we found out you need to put your ky in a slott inside the door to acivate the power to your room. We took a coffee stirrer and put it in the slot when we werer not in the room to keep th fan running. The beds are hard but if you are tired enough it did not matter much.The in room coffee pot was cracked and was not replaced during our stay so we could not make coffee in our room. But the coffeee at the restarant was not far away and was excellent.It took 30 sec to 5 min to get the key out of the door. It never got fixed. 1 of 3 lights in the bathroom was out the whole time we were there.The room problems were reported to the Apple rep but were never resolved. None the less we were happy with our room. We have been in much much worse.The Apple reps wanted to sell you only a few tours they have on their list. When I asked about a tour offered by another company they did not have on their list they made excuses why they did not sell them. When pressed they were still no help. While articulate and well informed, they did not serve their clients well.We did go on the Bavaro Runners and the Alto Chavon tours with favorable results.We would go back there again and would reccomend it to most everyone.

<Author>STARROSE1
<Content>Not Going Back to Natura Ours was a family vacation with 9 of us going including three children 14, 11 and 3. From Dec 21 to Dec 28. Shower, phone, TV, Air Conditioning.Restaurants- Buffet Restaurant not big enough during peak eating times. Very disorganized and long waits for the special stations provided.- Beach side restaurant for lunch was not bad, however very understaffed. The lady who cooked the hamburgers and hotdogs was the only person at that station and had to leave to get plates or more food. This restaurant also served as the International restaurant at night - we did not book this restaurant.- Italian Restaurant - not bad - the lasagne was delicious. Watch out, their version of a house salad includes Tuna.- A la Carte restaurants - book them right away. Don't wait until the last minute. Not happy when we tried to book 9 people at the Steak house - they told me no reservations for 9 people until 9pm - too late for my 3 year old. Some of the meat at the buffet was too tough.Animal Life - Expected more - geese, ducks, flamingos, fish - During the evening the birds are still around and can sometimes be pretty noisy while you are trying to sleep.Pool - The water was a little too cool, but you did get use to it. Not as big as I thought it would be. I don't care much for swim up bars as they are normally in the shade and it becomes too cold to stay.Entertainment - Very pleasant - some material not suitable for the kids. There was suppose to be a flea market down the beach at another resort within walking distance but it was removed. Too far to walk to the local town. There were vendors that come onto the resort to sell, but no clothing selections. You could only get T-shirts and other items in the gift shop which, as we all know, are quite expensive and there is no room for negotiation.Room Service - They tell you not to tip, but my husband and I leave a couple of dollars every day. We normally get okay service - not much to complain about - however, one day we almost didn't get towels.Check-in - Make sure you have everything - a number of guests did not receive their lockbox keys. This is very important. There were some guests who had their passports stolen.Staff - Overall everyone was very nice even though they were understaffed.Spa - Only utilized the service once for a family member. I booked an 80 min. massage for one day and the spa overbooked. It was split into two days. Very disappointed. I booked this way in advance.Scuba/Water Sports - the people here were quite knowledgeable and very safe - they ran a tight ship. Thanks Tania.The overall condition of the whole hotel needs a makeover. It's old and needs updating, repairs and upgrading, more staff, especially during a busy time.Unfortunately, we will not be going back to this resort, my husband and I are sure we can find better.
