<Author>jokerbee
<Content>Good relaxing time at Natura Park My girlfriend and I (both mid 20s) stayed at Natura Park during November. Overall, we had a great time there, and I will highlight some of the positives and negatives.Positives:(1) Room was nice and clean(2) The beach was absolutely perfect. Clean, clear, warm water to swim in. Plenty of chairs under really nice straw canopies. Was not crowded in Nov at all.(3) Pool was nice, again plenty of chairs available. Swim-up pool bar was an awesome feature.(4) Activities were good - we played volleyball, beach darts, and took a catamaran out to sea. Snorkeling and kayaks were available for free also.(5) Grounds were beautiful. Had a great time exploring all the different areas with cool trees and feeding all the fish in each pond.(6) Meals were generally good. The fruit smoothie and omelette station were the best breakfast items. The lunch buffett out by the beach wasn't as good each day. The dinners made up for them though, as you get to sign up for the italian, seafood, and steak restaurants, where the food was very good.(7) Great value given the relatively inexpensive cost for an all-inclusive resort.Negatives:(1) The bathroom door was pretty thin as some ppl have commented, but I didn't think it was that big a deal.(2) There was some seaweed on the shore. I didn't mind too much b/c there were workers constantly gathering it and shipping it away. The seaweed didn't even seem dirty, and I could always find a stretch of shore where it was clear.(3) Yes most of the workers only speak Spanish. If you are the type whose vacation is ruined if everyone (maid, waiters, etc) doesn't speak perfect English, then you probably shouldn't come here. I spoke no Spanish other than the 5-10 phrases I learned on the plane, my girlfriend had some knowledge of it from high school, and we had a great time.(4) The only negative about the meals was that there was an insect problem at the steakhouse, which sat right in the middle of a pond/lagoon. Definitely bring insect repellent. The waiters did their best to keep the insects away, but there's only so much you can do when you combine standing water with lights and food at night in a natural environment.(5) The nightlife was not their strength. They did their best to put on shows each night, but this is definitely not the greatest place to stay if you like to party all night. Lots of bars are open though.Overall, we had a great experience there. The small negatives mentioned didn't prevent us from enjoying ourselves immensely. Would definitely recommend Natura Park for anyone looking for a relaxing time at a unique resort with a great beachfront and stunning grounds.

<Author>Ann987
<Content>Very relaxing vacation We (my daughter, husband and me) just returned from a wonderful and relaxing vacation at Natura Park. This was the second time we traveled to Natura Park. GroundsVery nice, very well kept, yes there are birds but if you don鈥檛 disturb them they don鈥檛 bother you. We did feed them several times and we didn鈥檛 have any problems. RoomsCheck in went smoothly and we quickly got our key. The room is a little bit outdated but still very comfortable with good air conditioner, good washroom and nice beds. We even saw then replacing old bathtubs in other units. The only problem that we had was that the safe opens with a key and not a pass number. Normally that wouldn鈥檛 be much of a problem, except that we lost our key to the safe and it took them a while to drill the lock out because they didn鈥檛 have a spare key since each safe key is unique. One piece of advice is to make sure your keys are securely attached to a wristband or necklace.We did bring gifts for the maid (school supplies, shampoos, Tylenol, old clothes) and they really appreciate it. PoolWe never actually went inside since we spent most of the time in the sea but it seemed clean. BeachThe beach is amazing. The water is clear, no waves, white sand. We went snorkeling and we saw a great variety of fish on the reef. If you bring a piece of bread with you the fish eat right from your hand! We tried a lot of non-motorized sports (windsurfing, catamaran) and we really enjoyed them, they are all free, and if you are not sure they are lessons available. When we went there weren鈥檛 a lot of people at the resort so we had no problem getting chairs, although during peak periods it is probably not as easy.FoodThe food was good, a lot of variety, and most importantly no stomach problems. The food did not seem to be recycled through meals. During dinner we sometimes felt that the food was better at the buffet than at the a la carte restaurants because you could see what you pick and not blindly picking out of the menu. We did enjoy the a la carte restaurants and left tips, the best a la carte is the Italian where they have very tasty sauces and bread sticks.ShoppingWe did go shopping at the strip along the beach but the vendors are really pushy to get you to buy something so be prepared. If you want to get a good price say about 30% of the price they say and then agree on about 50%. We ended up later going to gift shop where we found a big variety with decent prices without the need to argue. Overall we found the vacation wonderful for the price we paid. We ended up not going on any excursions and just enjoyed the resort and the beach. When traveling you have to go with an open mind because there is no such thing as the perfect vacation and you will always find bumps along the way. The staff do try their best and are very friendly, their English is not perfect but remember that people not only come from Canada/US, they also come from Germany, France, Spain, so the staff have to know a lot of different languages. If you are looking for a very large, busy hotel with a lot of people than Natura Park is not right for you. Remember to keep an open mind because it is a different country with a different culture.

You can see that they were well trainned and are very professional (only the guy at the Gym + the night show entertainer + the swimming pool entertainner need a serious refresh in customer service).Special estrellas (stars) to:-Jose (at the towel-exchange booth).this gentleman is so entertainnning, fun that you'll forever remember him, believe me.-Rafael (bartender), Catalano (restaurant manager) are very professional, accomodating and devoted.I've been to all types of hotels (from the 5* Paradisus of Holguin, to some awesome Sandals, Accor, Iberostar, Melia hotels all around the globe), and I can safely say that Natura Park is a recommendable discrete nice cozy hotel ... they just need to improve the entertainment, add more flavour to their sea food restaurant and just buy the left side of their current beach location (if that's possible). PS: Big thumbs up to the travel carrier Sunwing since everything went well.

<Rating>1	3	1	2	1	1	3	-1	

<Author>VacationerMaine
<Content>Great Trip/travel tips We had a great vacation week at Natura Park and returned home on May 13th. We booked through AAA and they went through Apple vacations. The charter flight was direct and comfortable, with a movie and meal. I would travel with Apple again, they provide everything that their guests need. No worries! The buses were comfortable and air conditioned. Anytime we had a little problem at the hotel we mentioned Apple and the problem went away. When we arrived at the airport in Punta Cana our photo was taken with local women in bright dresses to purchase when we returned to the airport for departure for $8. So if you like that idea you may want to dress nicely, smile pretty, and have some cash with you when you return home to purchase it. The hotel was great. Many of the staff do not speak English but enough did that it was not a problem. The staff was friendly and helpful. Our room was nice with a big walk in closet and nice patio. Not a five star hotel but nice and clean. Each room has a safe for no extra fee and we used ours. They do not provide face cloths so you may want to pack some of those. The electricity in the room was not compatible with US plugs. They had mostly 220 outlets and one 110 in the bathroom but you need to bring an adapter to use US plugs in any of them. The adapters they sold in the gift shop were opposite what we needed so that was no help. There are no clocks in the rooms so you may want to bring a watch or travel alarm clock. A note about money: We brought traveller's checks but found them hard to use there. They could be cashed at the hotel for Dominican Pesos only with lots of ID and paperwork. The exchange rate was about 1 USD to 32 Pesos so the pesos were bulky to carry and didn't go far. US dollars were accepted and preferred everywhere so there was really no need to bother with the checks. Credit cards were only accepted for larger purchases. We brought lots of $1 and $5 for tippng and were glad we did. Next time we will bring more larger bills for shopping rather than planning to use ATM or travelers checks. The beach at the hotel was beautiful and the swimming excellent. There were beautiful fish to see under the water. Don't miss out on the snorkeling. A friend gave me a tip that worked really well. Fill an empty water bottle with bread then open it under water then watch the fish swarm you! It was so much fun that we bought a cheap underwater camera to photo the fish. You may want to bring one from home. We were surprised to learn that the water sports equipment was provided by another organization for the hotel. The staff at the water sport center were not very friendly and required a cash deposit before allowing us to use any equipment . The deposit for a snorkel and mask was $20 and no fins. We were required to return them in 1 hour even though they were not at all busy. I might have brought my own had I known. For the catamaran they first required payment for a lesson. The food was fine. Not gourmet, but we were not expecting that. The A-la-carte restaurants were good. The steak restaurant was our favorite. The tenderloin was better than the ribeye. We could only book each of the three restaurant once for our week stay but the buffets had lots of choices so we didn't mind. We read a tip from a few guests before our trip that suggested bringing a large cup to save trips to and from the bar for drinks and be more eco-friendly. That worked well for us. We brought the self insulated type that stay cool longer. We went to the beach after breakfast each day and had no trouble finding a beach chair with an umbrella. It was a pretty quiet week that we were there. The hotel had activities by the pool every day but we were just there for RR so didn't participate. There were many European guests on the beach so many women were topless. The beach has security all the time. Vendors do approach you when you are walking on the beach by all the hotels to offer to sell you excursions, timeshare tours, and lure you to their shops. They are polite and do leave you alone if you just tell them no thanks. The shops on the beach are fun to look in. The shop keepers don't take no for an answer though and will keep trying to make a deal until you leave.We booked one excursion through our Apple Rep to go to La Romana and Altos de Chavon. The Apple guides and bus drivers were great, but I wouldn't take that one again because it was far too much time on a bus. Altos de Chavon and the caves were fun but the boat ride was not great and the long time on the bus was tiring. It was interesting to learn about the country and we met some very nice people both Dominican and American. It is a very poor nation so tip well while you are there, and maybe bring some school supplies for a local school. If you are like me and always cold, don't bother packing sweaters because it is very hot there and all the hotel restaurants are open air. There is air conditioning in the bedrooms but it only brought the temp down to about 75. We had a great relaxing vacation at Natura Park and will definitely return again! My biggest decisions of each day were which bikini to wear and what the drink of the day would be. Now we are back to the work grind and wishing we were still there on the beach!

<Author>RelaxedNewBrunswick
<Content>8 Happy New Brunswickers Punta Cana - Natura Park Beach - Eco Resort  SpaWe were a group of 8 ladies from New Brunswick looking for a relaxing vacation. We found it. We could not have had a better time. We were there March 26-April 2/07. The resort was very beautiful, very well maintained. You will not find a harder working staff anywhere. The rooms were great, very spacious and very clean. The maids did a great job. The staff were very friendly and helpful. The service was great . If there was a problem of any type it was corrected very promptly. The food was good. The buffet was very nice with so many selections even the most fussy person could find something they could eat. The pasta bar was great. Lots of fresh fruit and many desserts.The breakfast was very good with a smoothie bar and fresh omelets every morning and everything you could ever imagine and more.. The best a la cart was the steak restaurant. The other 2 not so good. The drinks were great and the bartenders were friendly. This is very important as we have found from other not so great trips. We didn't find any language barrier and none of us spoke Spanish. The pool was very nice, well kept and a good size. The beach was the best. The seaweed was raked up every day. Other resort beaches to the right of ours were not raked or looked after at all. Ours was by far the nicest and very well kept. Yes, you have to save a lounge chair early if you want to have a seat and or some shade for the day but there are lots of lounges and quite a few grass huts. There are two small bars right on the beach which was great. Bring your own thermal cup and they will gladly fill it for you. The beach grill was great. We had lunch there every day but one. We read some very bad reviews before we left and were a little concerned but honestly we cannot understand all of the complaints. It is a very relaxing and beautlful place. We would highly recommend it. But...it definately is not a swinging resort for young, party animals. Our ages range was 30ish to 60ish. In fact as a group, the only 2 areas of improvement we could see were the nightly entertainment. They really need some help in this area. And the other was that very seldom was there a bartender at the swim-up bar. However the bar above it was always open but its just a little special to swim up and sit and have a drink on your vacation. Regardless, it was a great vacation.

<Author>95oRANGEcRUSH
<Content>Wonderful time had by all!! Myself and my two friends ( all 23 years old) traveled to this resort the 17th of March thru the 24th of March. I can speak basic Spanish, while both of my friends knew nothing in Spanish. Knowing simple phrases like I want, please, hi, how are you?, thanks, etc really goes along way. Some of the staff (bartenders, front desk, Entertainment staff) spoke quite a bit of English, however, making an attempt to speak Spanish will definitely earn you respect from the staff. So climb out of your shell a bit, remember it's vacation, and have fun trying new things.Let me say that we experienced none of the problems that some of the other reviewers had on here. I don't know if these people are royalty (sarcasm) or if they are normally crabby people to begin with, but, I find their reviews to be highly (read: overtly over dramatic) of their 'horrible' time. During our week at Natura Park the guests were primarily from various European countries. Spain, Italy, France, etc. I thought Americans were rude, but, it turns out that the people from Euro nations were horrible. They would cut in line at the buffet and showed no courtesy to others. This was the only drawback to our trip, so if you have little patience for others be forwarned!!The food was fine. I have a sensitive stomach. I took a new bottle of Pepto with me and never had to open it. Take Immodium or Pepto just in case, everybody reacts differently to changes in their diet. The buffet had all kinds of foods, enough to conquer the hunger of even the pickiest eaters. You can get smoothies at breakfast in the morning that are made from fresh fruit. They have chefs during the meals to make omelets to your liking, carve beef, etc. There is a chef on the beach who makes lunch daily and it is delicious!! My buddy had quite a time feasting on ribs one afternoon!! A la carte dinners were ok. Lobster was ok, steak ok. The staff try really hard to make it an elegant time, so be respectful and appreciate their efforts. Our hotel room (1132) was located in patio 11, I'm pretty sure. The room had two double beds, clean bathroom, fullsize couch, color tv, tile flooring, etc. Our room was ground level and the patio looked out over a nicely manicured lawn and landscaping. We tipped our maid $2/day and she kept our room spotless. Our beds were made and had some type of flower poking out on top which was a nice touch! Room was fine; no ants or roaches! Plus, they have a pest control team that sprays weekly for insects, so don't worry about bugs. Daytime and Nightime entertainment were a blast. Yes, it is not Vegas quality entertainment, but, it is what you make of it! If you want to be grumpy and hate the entertainment then that is your choice, but we had a blast with the entertainment staff. They encourage you to participate and try to get you involved. Remember, it is vacation, let loose and have fun! The grounds are very well taken care of. Any trash you see laying around is from the tourists, NOT THE DOMINICANS!! So do your part and keep paradise beautiful. Oh, and about paradise. The week we went it was 95 and sunny everyday!! Bring lots of sunblock and a bottle of aloe gel. Anything you don't protect will get burnt!! This isn't like going to Florida or Myrtle Beach, you're much closer to the Equator and the sun is much hotter and stronger!! There is a breeze all day and night which makes it very nice.Now, seeing as we are 23 and finishing college you know we did some drinking. The beers in the hotel room (Quesaquia, spelling is off) are not too good. After 1 or 2 it is fine, but not great. The Presidente beer is pretty good, in my opinion. Tastes close to Budweiser. Mixed drinks are a dime a dozen, meaning they know quite a variety to make. Almost all of the mixed drinks contain rum, and their rum is very good and strong!! It will take several drinks to feel the effects of the alcohol, so drink up and be happy! Francesco is the bartender in the second level of the pool bar. He is a great bartender, so try everything the menu offers!! Tips are another area of concern with travelers. Remember, tips are included in your all-inclusive. However, if you see what the country looks like outside of the resort you will realize that you should do a little tipping to be generous. How much is up to you, but I did the following. Tipped the maid $2/day, bartender(s) $1-2 every other or every 3rd trip to the bar, a la carte dinners $2-3. How much is up to you so plan accordingly. There is no hurry in the Caribbean. So please, don't be that antsy and impatient person demanding room service bring you towels right away or whatever demands you may think need to be met immediately. The staff takes their time, and a common expression you will hear is Ok, no worries. For example, our maid only left 2 towels after cleaning our room and we needed 3. I politely told her and she said another 5 minutes and we would get another one. 5 minutes came and went, so we went to the beach and did our thing without worrying about the towel. When we came back later to take our showers there were 3 towels. And that is exactly the mentality you should have. Leave school, work, and other problems where you come from and enjoy your trip. Not only will you get more out of your trip, but others will enjoy theirs a little more, too. Always barter with the vendors about a mile down the beach and to the right. They will throw a high price at first, but will usually sell for less than half of the initial price. When looking out at the ocean, turn left and walk 1-2 miles down. The swimming is much better where it is a sandy bottom and you can get right next to some small reef systems and see many colorful saltwater fish. Also, take a few bread rolls from the outside buffet by the beach at lunch and go out in the water and feed the fish. It is quite the experience!! Check out the marinarium adventure if you want to snorkel and swim with sting rays and nurse sharks; very fun!!This is not a good place to go if you are single between the ages of 16-30 and looking to find romance. It is primarily a baby boomer crowd and young families. However, if you want a great place to unwind then this is it.

<Author>vylent
<Content>Very nice hotel and beach, friendly staff, disappointing a la carte restaurants We booked our trip through USA3000 Vacations who is affiliated with Apple Vacations. I do not know if we saved any money, but we received all the perks that the people who travelled with Apple Vacations received.At the Punta Cana International Airport, you have to pay $10 as an Airport fee. (If you book with Apple, you do not have to pay the $20 departure fee, but everyone else, you will have to pay the $20 when leaving).After the bus ride to the hotel, we arrived at 12:30, but had to wait around for half an hour till we got our room. The front desk people are very nice, especially the women. We got stuck with some young guy who had no idea what we were saying.The rooms are nice and clean. We brought $200 in singles with us, and it helped with the tipping and the bargaining (change carries some weight with the vendors).The beach is nice, and the entertainment guys are really nice as well. The staff is always smiling and singing random songs as they day goes by. The bars are very limited, but the local rum (barcelo) isnt that bad. In fact, we brought some back with us.Now the only part that was disappointing was the seafood a la carte restaurant. There are only 3, and since we only stayed 7 nights, they only allowed us to book 2. The people Apple book the restaurants for you, so that you dont have to go through the hassle, but if you want to change the reservations, the guest services desk is really nice and will help you out.We booked our excursions through the Apple rep, and went on a 4x4 trip around some of Punta Cana and went to Saona Island which looks like paradise in the middle of no-where. Both of the trips were well worth it.Just a few things to check: 1. Tip everyone you acquire services from, you will notice how much they appreciate it and they will take good care of you. 2. For souveneirs, dont go to the hotel gift shop. Walk down the beach to the right where there are some shops. It is a bit high pressure, but you can bargain for just about anything. 3. Take some excursions, you will want to get out of the resort atleast once. 4. Avoid late night reservations, thats when we were very weary of the food at the a la carte restaurant.All in all, it was a pretty good place, and I would come back to Punta Cana, but I would want to experience another hotel.

<Author>swimmerEvanston
<Content>Do motor boats really need to come this close to the beach? We stayed at Natura Park during the first week of February.We found staff to be helpful and friendly and very hard-working. The food - while not gourmet - was good enough. After all, we came for the sun and the swimming and not to get fat. The grounds are beautiful and very well kept.But I like to swim in the ocean and found the designated (roped-off) area much too small and weedy. Swimming outside the designated area where there are large kelp beds and wild-life (fish and large turtles) and hardly any floating weeds was much too dangerous because of the nearly constant traffic of motor boats. These boats with their noise and stinky exhaust fumes would come as close as just a few meters off the beach.My question: why do boats that can go just about anywhere have to come this close to the shore? Should not the beach and a reasonable distance out be reserved for swimmers? Why does the enjoyment of people on the beach have to be disrupted by the noise and stink from inconsiderate motor boaters? I feel very strongly that the immediate area off the beach - at least about 300 meters - should be off-limits to motor boats so that swimmers can be safe and this limit should be enforced and designated with buoys. I realize that the hotel may not be able to bring about a rule to keep motor boats a safe distance from swimmers. Cooperation among resorts may be necessary to bring this about. But I think it would be in the interest of the Dominican Republic AND the resorts to make sure that swimmers be safe from being run down and injured or killed by motor boats.We will certainly NOT return to Natura Park or visit any other resort where we cannot safely swim in the ocean near the resort.Other than this I feel we got our money's worth.

This may actually have been a blessing for anyone who actually likes half decent wine since it's beyond terrible as is the beer. I would have been happy to pay for good wine or beer, I'm not a big drinker but do appreciate a nice glass of wine with dinner or the odd beer on the beach. <Author>travels_with_kidsAyr
<Content>Great vacation in the Sun We stayed at Natura Park Jan 11-18, 2007 and we had a great time. There is always something to complain about if you want to, but it was definitely a nice resort.We travelled with another family and had 4 children between us (ages 5, 7, 9 11). The kids were feeling a bit too old for the Kids Club but did participate in the Mini Disco show when they could. Petra was nice and did invite the kids to the club. Jimy encouraged the kids to participate in daily activities at the pool and on the beach. He was very friendly. They had sand toys and games by the pool - shuffleboard, mini-golf, bean bag toss etc.The beach did have seaweed. What built up over the day was collected each morning, so it wasn't horrible. There seemed to be more build up on the hotels next door (Allegro, Punta Cana Grand). We spent most of our time at the pool - though the older kids did some snorkelling. It was windy - so the ocean was wavy but the breeze was nice. It did bring in some clouds - and sunshowers, but really only lasted a minute or two.The rooms were average and we got good maid service. We did not use anything in the Mini Bar because we didn't need to. We had plenty of towels, soap etc. We got lots of water in big bottles every day.Don't buy from the vendors (sharks) that come on to the resort. They wear pink/peach shirts and hound you if you are around the pool. You can get much better deals at the hotel gift shop or if you feel like bargaining there is a market down the beach at the Punta Cana Grand (to the right). But beware, they will all want you to visit their shop for the cheapie, cheapie deals. Just be prepared to haggle or say no. We ate at all the restaurants -including the beach grill and none of us got sick. We liked the smoothie bar at the main buffet. But there was always a wait.The resort was getting busier as our week progressed and we did have to line up for lunch at the main buffet one day (I think they weren't able to clean up tables fast enough) and the pool restaurant was more crowded. But really what is the rush if you are on vacation?DO NOT change any money into Dominican Pesos. Everywhere takes US dollars and you can't change the Pesos back to any other currency. DO NOT take the bus to the Palma Real shopping center. It took over 40 minutes with all the stops at other hotels and there were only 4 stores open. It will be nice when it is done, but give it another year or so.DO take a bun and feed the turtles at the bridge at the front entrance. It is a hoot to watch the turtles, ducks and fish fight for the food. They all seem to come out of nowhere.DO take the country adventure/safari trip. We went with County Adventures - there are lots of tour companies that do it. You get to see a Dominican home, a school, a sugar plantation, a coffee/cocoa ranch, have a horsback ride and boogie board at a beautiful beach. (And the requisite stop at a tourist gift shop - with items made in China). The kids really learned a lot about how easy they have it. Also we took some school supplies to leave at the school (pens, pencils, erasers, crayons, notebooks etc). Enough said. Enjoy the quietness of the resort. There are no other attractions (other than a Casino) around, so you will relax. Take sunscreen and bug spray (we did have mosquitos at the Italian a la carte one night - but otherwise none).

<Author>coachnhs
<Content>Solid Lodgings First of all,let me say that some of the negative comments made by travelers on this website were a tad outrageous. Comments about the beds being to close to the floor, bathroom door not being soundproof, small bars of soap, etc. are pretty miniscule at best.Other legitimate complaints concerning poor service, excessive bug infestations,dirty pool and beach made me second guess our choice of Natura Park for our first visit to Punta Cana. While we don't consider Natura Park a 5* hotel, our 4 day stay was quite enjoyable to say the least. The service, pool, and grounds were above average, while the food, room, and beach were average. <Author>Sunshine_in_the_Snow
<Content>Loved it! Date of stay: January 06-13, 2007I loved it. It was a very quiet and relaxing vacation. The food was good. Even my husband, a picky eater, didn't have a problem. The room was very clean. All of the staff were friendly and very eager to help out any way they could. The little bit of Spanish I have came in handy, but almost all spoke enough English to manage. The water pressure was an unexpected bonus. I didn't hear of anyone being sick during our stay. You should keep in mind while indulging of the all inclusive drinks and food that coconuts and bananas are a natural laxative....We found that the beach just a two minute walk to the left of the resort to be a wonderful secret snorkel spot. We took our snorkel gear, buns and bananas and snorkeled every day.It rained for about 5 minutes at a time a couple of times a day. ...sunshower really. I just stayed where I was and enjoyed the refreshing sprinkle. It was funny to see some grab their towels and run for cover to have it stop by the time they got under cover.Getting beach chairs was certainly a challenge for those who partied late and didn't get up until late morning. ...the early bird gets the worm!I can't comment on the entertainment. I missed it all. That was one complaint I have... The adult shows didn't start until 9:45. We were usually wiped from a full day of sun, swimming and fresh air to be bothered to stay up until 9:45 waiting for the shows.I recommend Dolphin Island (swimming with the dolphins). It was quite expensive, but I did enjoy it. I paid $95 US. It's a three hour excursion, about half hour of that is actually with the dolphins. Some of that half hour is watching others, but you are in the water with them.We also really enjoyed a two hour horse back ride with Pandora along the ocean. Those wonderful towel guys at Natura will tell you all about that excursion.We didn't officially pay for an open jeep tour, but ended up having one any way. The truck that picked us up for the horse ranch got run off the road by a bigger truck and we nearly tipped over and then the road to the ranch was so bumpy we figured we got our jeep tour when we paid for our horse back riding.The bus ride to and from the resort is another adventure on its own. The bigger the vehicle, the more daring the driver seems to be on those narrow winding roads. What a ride! Well worth a tip.After reading several of the January 03rd reviews immediately before my trip I was worried that I had made a mistake. Thank you Toronto for your review. I've come to appreciate the reviews of my fellow Canadians. They are closer to my own expectations. I totally agree with your review that some people are just born complainers. A five star hotel in the Caribbean is not Trump Towers. If one doesn't like seaweed on the beach, then stay away from the ocean! It isn't the locals who leave their cups, straws and other garbage on the beach and around the grounds - it's the ignorant tourist! If the closet door doesn't close it doesn't make the vacation awful unless you want it to be. We had a shower curtain where the end kept coming out of the track. A wad of chewing gum allowed to dry in the track fixed it just nicely!I loved seeing and feeding the geese, flamingos, peacock, fish and turtles every day. The grounds were absolutely beautiful. Remember to pocket a couple of buns at lunch and dinner and a banana at breakfast to feed them all.If you consider yourself easy going and enjoy nature - Go ahead - book your vacation with Natura Park. You'll love it too!

<Author>Yus-Weasi
<Content>Go at own risk - and then with low expectations I'm so happy to see other reviews that could very well be my own. My husband and I set our expectations low to begin with so we wouldn't be disappointed. All we really wanted to do was get away for 3 days. We thought it would be cool to try an all-inclusive and imagined ourselves in a Corona commercial munching on some yummy tropical food. Well, we will never do another all-inclusive and next time I go to any resort, I'm packing peanut butter and jelly; and 2 boxes of Immodium instead of 1.We were pleasantly surprised by the architecture of the main building and the grounds. We were also surprised by the 20 mph winds coming in off the beach. Obviously we can't fault them for Mother's Nature nature but a write-up somewhere would have been nice.We can, however, fault them for the nastiest food I've ever tasted and I'm comparing this to summer camps, college dorm food and an Outward Bound trip where I ate rehydrated black beans and powdered pasta sauce. Considering food is a large part of the all-inclusive appeal - we were seriously ripped off.We were never able to get reservations to the restaurants even though they weren't full every night. So we ate at the buffet for 3 days. After day 1 we learned to stick to the bread, rice and pasta but still were hit with some intestinal thing (1 week later we both still have aftershocks). Maybe it's from the guy who licked his hands while grilling the hotdogs and hamburgers. Or it could be from the server who merely turned table cloths over instead of getting clean ones (she also drank out of the leftover wine bottles and ate leftover food off people's plates). Or maybe it was from the dirty silverware, glasses and dishes. Or maybe from people touching my food with their bare hands. Let's all be thankful for the FDA.Though I was suprised by the lack of English spoken, I enjoyed the opportunity to reach into the recesses of my brain for those ol' Spanish classes I took in college. However, it was frustrating at times when it shouldn't have been. And the service was not good. We expected slow service because we have traveled in the caribbean before but there was virtually no service here.The rooms could use some updating but like I said, we set our expectations low so we were pleased there were no bugs or mildew. We did enjoy how international the resort was and the variety show was so bad you had to watch - but I loved that aspect.I would have a hard time recommending anyone go to Punta Cana. There are so many other great places to visit. What scares me are the people who think Natura Park is the greatest place on earth. What's wrong with you?! My favorite caribbean destination is St. Lucia. The Jalousie was a little slice of heaven and once the construction is done at the Windjammer, it probably won't be bad either.

<Author>suntravellor
<Content>Excellent Vacation We were at Natura from Boxing Day to Jan. 2. Check in at the resort was chaos. Apparently there had been some damaged rooms the night before from some unruly guests, in addition to the hotel being overbooked, which resulted in re-locating a number of guests to another resort. The rooms were not ready at 3:00 p.m. which was the promised check in time. A number of guests were getting quite irate by 5 p.m. when they still didn't have rooms. But nothing says you have to sit in the lobby fuming about it. We enjoyed the buffet, the beach and the bars until we had a room. That is why you pack your bathing suit in your carry on. The rooms are spacious and clean. We didn't come to a tropical island in December to have the air conditioning on, but ours did work. We would turn it off and the maid always put it back on, but it kept the room smelling fresher. The shower was fine, sometimes no hot water, but when you have a 1000 people trying to shower all at the same time, you can expect to run out, it happens at home after five people shower in a household. The meals at the buffet were fine. Not overwhelming with selection, but tasty none the less. (tasted like home - Canada) The al a carte meals were fantastic . Service in the Italian restaurant was terrible, but the food made up for it. And we had great entertainment, as a giant cockroach did laps, circling the very top of the buffet table, until a young lady attempted to help herself to salad at the exact time the cockroach decided to come down for a closer look at the food. She nearly dropped her plate and ran from the table. Another guest became hysterical and left crying, before the meal arrived. I don't like cockroaches any more than the next person, but this is a tropical island in an open air restaurant and I am sure the same could happen anywhere, especially when you don't have cold weather controlling the size of bugs. The roof leaked in one section of the buffet and during a heavy rainstorm water poured in this area creating a pool on the marble floor, making it extremely dangerous for walking. There were plenty of other seats available, which they overlooked and put people in this wet area. Management does not seem too on the ball. The other two al a cartes more than made up for the Itallian with unbelievable service and quality of food. Yes, the portions are smaller, but more than adequate for a meal.The drinks were tasty and bar service was fine. We had no language problems at all and in fact were pleasantly surprised at the level of English spoken by the staff . The beach is beautiful, the water is beautiful, the weather was beautiful. We took a day trip to Saona for $85 US each, which we felt was more than worth the money. We left at 8 a.m. and weren't back until 7 ish. We travelled by air conditioned bus, catamaran, and speed boat and saw lots of sites, were entertained by locals, had an excellent lunch and probably some of the best snorkelling we have done and we have snorkelled in the Mayan Riviera, Cozumel, Sossua, and Jamaica. Our last visit to Dominican was four years ago, and it has grown up a lot since then. The weather was in the 30's everyday and for this time of year, that is fantastic in my mind for a Christmas vacation. We may have to make the Dominican Republic an annual winter event. We wouldn't return to Natura, but only because there is so much out there to see and experience. I would recommend this resort to anyone as long as you go with the mind set, it is a tropical country, different than the place you are leaving behind, and be open to new experiences.

<Author>88.fingers.ca
<Content>It must be a terrible place to work! Stayed there from Dec 26/06 to Jan 2/07. I have been to Punta Cana once before at an excellent resort, and my wife has been to several resorts in Punta Cana and Puerto Plata, as well as Acapulco, Mexico, etc. I regret that there is a lot of negativity in this review, I still had a great time in spite of the resort (thanks to the weather, the beautiful beach and my 16-mo. old daughter's laughter).First the good stuff:I liked the rooms, the resort grounds are beautiful, the food at the steakhouse was very good and the New Year's Eve dinner was also very good. None of us got sick, although my daughter had a mild bout of diarrhea before we switched her to rice, pasta, water, bananas and some fruit. The staff was pretty good at raking up the seaweed from the beach, but they missed a day here and there. Weather was fantastic, poured like hell most nights and gorgeous breezy days.But...We had all kinds of negative experiences with the service. The staff at the reception desk lied to us without blinking an eye, first about when the rooms would be ready and again about finding a crib for our daughter. In my opinion, it appears they are trained to tell you whatever you want to hear so you will go away and stop bothering them. While the clerk I was speaking with insisted she never said to come back for our room keys at 2:30, that check-in time is 3, the clerk beside her was having a similar conversation, insisting with a smile that he told my fellow traveller that keys would be ready at 3:30. This made my clerk a little uncomfortable, since they were both telling different stories. Others from our flight (arrived in PC at 10.30am) didn't get their room keys until 5.30pm.On check-in (1pm) we asked a crib for my 16 mo. old daughter. At 8.30pm when we didn't have one yet, I went to the front desk to ask for one, and was told we would have one in 20 minutes. 90 minutes later I went back to the front desk and asked where it was, could we go to housekeeping and find one. The same person behind the desk explained to me that a crib wasn't part of our reservation. I lost it. I realize now that their blank stares were indications that they simply didn't understand what I was asking. Eventually they said they would try and locate one, and the manager (? - could have been anybody since he didn't identify himself) said he would call us in the room to make sure we got one. He never called. An hour later I found one in a hallway and carried it to our room. When we related our frustration to the Sunwing tour rep, he went and talked to the front desk, returned and apologized on the behalf of Natura. He also said they would make it up to us with some sort of detail - a bottle of rum or something. Nada, never heard from them again. All this on our first day.Language barriers abounded; I fully appreciate that Spanish is the native tongue, but keep in mind I wasn't backpacking in the Dominican - this is an all-inclusive and, to some degree, you rely on the staff to make the effort to help you have a good time. I had no such problems at my last resort (Bavaro Princess). Nada from this resort. I did the best I could with Spanish, but when I had to rely on English to try and ask/explain something, I didn't get anywhere with anyone.Bellhops, waiters, bus staff, bartenders, some housekeepers - nobody wanted to do more than the bare minimum. There was even some rudeness. We gave up asking for cutlery/napkins/coffee refills: it was so much easier to wander around La Cana (the main buffet rest.) until you found it yourself. Twice I had to go hunting for towels because the housekeeper forgot us. On one of those occasions, I called the front desk, tried to explain that we had no towels, they said they would take care of it. An hour later a maintenance guy showed up to fix the door. (--?!) Thankfully, he had a key to the housekeeping linen closet and brought us two bath towels. The wind frequently blew debris into the pool from the beach restaurant. As the day went on, I was surprised that no staff came along to clean it up. Paper napkins, bits of food, dirt, etc. accumulated at the two ramps leading into the pool (The ramps are great for toddlers!). The foot-washing showers to remove sand were broken. Lots of sand in the pool. I developed a sinus infection and my daughter a mild eye infection. Hard to say if it was from the pool, but I don't know where else either one of us would have picked it up.A friend we met on the plane to Punta Cana got violently ill - food poisoning - on his last meal before getting on the plane home. Poor guy spent the entire trip locked in the bathroom, paramedics waiting for him at the airport.There are better resorts for the same money. I'm willing to bet there are better resorts for less money. If you are desperate enough to get away and have to go here, then I hope you have no issues on your trip, otherwise you will be challenged to get any help: expect to fall between the cracks. Everyone else that I met (Canadians, French, Polish, Czech, German, Italian) all told the same familiar story. They said they wouldn't go back either. Sunwing will be my last choice for future trips.

<Author>NycNight_owl

<Author>NoneColumbus
<Content>Beautiful, friendly (for the most part) but one problem after another We have done Apple for Cancun and Apple for Punta Cana. Skip this one and go to Cancun. You will get a lot more for your money.First. the good part. It is a beautiful place and the staff is mostly very friendly, even when they are promising you faithfully that they will do something for you that they have absolutely no intention of doing. The beach is nice and there was no toplessness. The pool is nice. There were no insects. They accept American money, even out on the economy, so there is no need to change money. The weather couldn't have been better. No problems with European guests. They were very nice and many spoke English. We did not get sick, as we almost always do in Mexico.Now the bad part. There is a drumbeat of one maddening annoyance after another. They cut corners shamelessly on all the included stuff and the non-included stuff is very expensive.We flew out of Cleveland and had to get up at 3:30 in the morning to make our flight. We arrived at Natura Park at about eleven local time. By the time we got through the check-in line it was 11:30 local time, and we were dead, dead tired. The clerk told us that our room would not be ready until 1:00 and we should go and get something to eat. He told us to put our luggage in an unlocked storage room out of the view of the main desk, along with all the rest of the new arrivals. When we can back at 1:00, the same clerk said the check in time was 3:00 and he about bit my wife's head off when she mentioned that he had said 1:00. However, that was the only time anyone was rude to us there. The chairs in the lobby were very uncomfortable. It was well past 3:00 before we got our room. The room was mostly alright. It had a very large bed that was very hard. The air conditioning was adequate. The toilet wouldn't flush. They fixed that right away, but it ran loudly the whole time we were there. There was only one electrical outlet in the room that shared the very small and very dim television in the room with the coffee maker and my lap top computer. It took a constant stream of requests to get coffee for the coffee maker. You had to reach past exposed wires to get to the outlet. There was an ice bucket, but no ice machine anywhere. I can't imagine what the place would be like if you did not speak Spanish, which I do -- very well. The maid promised us over and over again to bring us ice, but never did. The place is in the middle of no where. You can't get off the premises without expensive transportation. The cab was twenty dollars each way and all I saw off premises was shops that sold poor quality tourist stuff.The tap water by all accounts is deadly. There were two large bottles of water in the room, but no way to chill them, because they were too big to fit in the minibar. If one had any water at all in it, the maid would not replace it. We ran out one night. They promised to send us another, but did not. We started hiding any part full water bottle from the maid, so we wouldn't run out again. The minibar is advertised as including free beverages. It contained one local beer and three bottles of Pepsi, which often did not get replaced until after making a big issue of it with two or three different people. It seemed like we got the best results when we went to the front desk and made an issue of it in person.The Apple representative said that there would be a briefing at 5:00 that evening. The briefing turned out to be a one on one pitch to sell tours. I did order the Santo Domingo Tour. My wife did not want to go, so I told the English challenged representative that I only wanted one. Then, she got on the phone and I heard her order two in Spanish. Since the amount that went on our credit card was in pesos and there was a big deal about that there were absolutely no refunds, that one might have gotten by someone who didn't understand Spanish. I was glad I went. It got me off the premises. However, they went to three tourist shops I can remember in Santo Domingo, not to mention the two stops they made on the road coming and going. Each visit lasted a good half hour, with two or three people shopping and everyone else grumbling out on the sidewalk. The shoe shine boys were very aggressive. If you didn't watch them, they would put a dab of polish on your shoe, including one poor guy in tennis shoes. Many of the sites were just drivebys, in traffic, with instructions to go to that side of the bus and take pictures out the window. We left before light and returned after dark.The buffet food was about nursing home quality. With some exceptions, the fresh fruit was unripe, hard and sour. The meat items were often very tough and tasteless. The deserts were very good, including four kinds of decent ice cream. The individually prepared breakfast omelet was very good. You have to make appointments to go to the restaurants. We went to the Perla first which is the seafood restaurant. I ordered a lobster, which came as a baked half. It was about the best I ever ate. My wife ordered something I forget, but did not like it. The sides and deserts were very Spartan. The Italian restaurant was ever worse. We got some sort of Italian named beef item that was very small and very tough. We went back to the Perla New Year's eve in the hopes of getting that lobster again. However, all they served was a tough and tasteless beef item, some boiled vegetables, a dot of sherbet and a hard to eat chocolate covered pear. We left hungry and it was too late to get to the buffet.The day we left, we had to be in the lobby at 7:30 that morning. When we got to the airport, the Apple representative made a long, hard sell pitch for tips, for him and the driver, with quite a guilt trip speech about how underpaid they were and how much they needed the money. Then, he and the driver stood on each side of the bus the door and glared at everyone as they got off the bus. I wonder if Apple knows he's doing that. At the airport, they put us in a line to check in. More hurry up and wait. There were people at all the counters, standing around and shooting the bull. However, for some inexplicable reason, they kept everyone standing in that line for some 45 minutes before they started checking people in. Our boarding pass said we were to go to gate 7. However, the guy standing there said it was really gate 5. That made no difference, because they were next to each other. A small machine made cup of watery coffee cost $2. A box of Pringles and a bottle of fruit juice cost more than $9. There was no one manning the counters. The plane was supposed to leave at 10:55. When it got to be 9:30 and no one appeared, it was obvious something was wrong. All the passengers waiting to board there were getting very worried, saying things like They can't go without us and someone else saying, Don't count on it! The airport has no information desk. I went to the other side of the airport where there was a plane boarding for Philadelphia. However, the guy at that station looked at my boarding pass and assured me solemnly that it really was gate 5 where I should be. 10:55 came and went. I and many others kept crossing the airport over and over again checking the gate that was boarding people and was staffed. No one ever did show up at gate 7. Finally, some 45 minutes later, someone said he had heard that we were boarding over at the other side of the airport. Everyone rushed over there and sure enough, they did board the flight back to Cleveland, some two hours late. They said the gates had been changed for security reasons. The captain said the flight had been delayed by a couple of brief rain showers that morning.You know, the thing that symbolizes the whole miserable experience is that ice bucket in the room and no way to get ice. Much promise. Little, if any, performance. Avoid this place. As long winded as all that was, it wasn't the half of it.

<Author>lizzylibrarian
<Content>Can't wait to go back! We stayed at Natura Park for three nights in August, 2006. It was an Apple Vacation that we booked through a travel agent. We had an absolutely wonderful time. Before we left I read the reviews on this site and took the advice of other reviewers re: bug spray, lots of $1 bills and taking coozies to keep our drinks cool, etc.We arrived at our hotel about 30 min. after leaving the airport. Our check in was very comprehensive and the staff was very good at explaining the mini bar (what was included, what wasn't etc.) and how to turn on the power in the room.A porter carried our bags to the room and showed us everything in the room. Everything was very clean and the room was practically freezing when we got there and stayed freezing throughout our stay. The power had been kept on by a brochure that was already in the slot by the door.We never lost power nor lost hot water while we were there. We also never had a problem communicating in the resort. My husband and I learned the basics but are really not Spanish speakers. But keep in mind you are in a spanish-speaking country, staying at a resort owned by Spaniards in which I would estimate 95% of the guests are Spanish speaking. It will serve you well to learn some Spanish. We are all guests in their country and should act accordingly.My husband, the picky one, LOVED the food, I thought it was okay. I certainly could always find something that I liked, even if I didn't know exactly what it was. My husband had no bowel problems. I did, but nothing major. (Immodium was my friend!) Since my husband practically gorged himself at every meal and had no problems, I think my problems were more due to the fact that the food was different, than it was that the food was spoiled or bad. We ate at the Seafood a la carte restaurant. It was wonderful. The lobster was awesome!We went on the Apple excursion to Santo Domingo. It's a long drive, but I loved it. We saw a lot of the country along the way. And Santo Domingo is of course amazing. I wished the excursion were longer, and I wished we had more free time in the city, but they work very hard to get you from A to B to see as much as you can in so little time. I suggest visitors take sunscreen with an SPF of *at least* 30, if not 50 or 60. Dominican Republic + August = HOT sun. We met a woman who had worn SPF 15 the day before, and was a tomato. I wore 30 and my very fair husband wore 50 and we had no problems. Apply often!I have read some complaints about the room number on the key. That is not exactly true. The number is on the key fob, so all you have to do is separate the fob from the key ring, and Bob's your uncle! We just put the fob in the slot on the wall to keep the A/C on. And we put our safe key on the same ring with our room key.I also read a review that in effect said if anyone had a rave review of this resort it is because they have never stayed at another resort. That is also not true. I have stayed at much fancier places, but YOU GET WHAT YOU PAY FOR. I could not believe how inexpensive our trip was and kept that in mind while I was there. I have paid much much more for other vacations and stayed at *much* fancier hotels but was not always impressed because I did not think I got what I paid for. At Natura Park you get more than what you've paid for, in my opinion. If you are used to top notch resorts, or require resorts that cater to Americans, this place is probably not for you. I honestly loved the evening entertainment. It indeed was cheesy, but also cute and fun. I was never bothered by them when they did stuff by the pool, and in fact thought it was great. But if you do think you might be bothered by them, all you have to do is walk down the beach a little ways and you can't really hear any music at the pool. My husband and I are late risers and never had a problem getting a chair either by the pool or on the beach under a hut because we didn't go out until after lunch. We loved both the pool and the beach.The only true complaint we have about our trip was our Apple representative, not Natura Park itself. Jaison, our Apple rep's only day off was Sunday. We left on Monday. Apple/USA 3000 flights are confirmed the day before they leave. Jaison told us he would call on Sunday to confirm our flight. Of course he never called and he didn't answer his cell when we called. Of course we simply assumed that our flight was still on but we were concerned because the pick-up time seemed extraordinarily early. Another couple that was in the same boat as us asked about sharing a cab the next morning so we could sleep a bit longer. Wimpy me was nervous about not towing the line so we just got up super early and got the Apple shuttle. Boy am I glad we did!!! Since the USA 3000 flights are essentially Apple flights they have their own way of doing things. Basically they get all the passengers on the same flight at the airport at the same time and check-in is done by flight. I'm not sure what happens if they close your flight's check-in before you get there, but I did see some close calls for passengers who missed their Apple shuttle. Long story short, even though we were at the airport super early, our flight ended up leaving 40 min. early too.We are now so excited to know that paradise is now only a 3.5 hr. direct flight from our house! We truly cannot wait to go back! We may try another resort, but for the right price would not hesitate to go back to Natura Park!

<Author>okguerita
<Content>Do you really want to get away? Then this is the place. Two friends and I stayed for 3 nights at the Natura (24-26 Aug 2006). This resort provided the perfect long-weekend escape we'd hoped for.UPSHOT- While not the fanciest resort in the area, Natura provides a laid-back atmosphere, a lovely beach, many activities for the whole family - and the opportunity for guests from the USA to really get away from the everyday. A vast majority of our fellow guests were from Spain (~90%), with the remaining 10% from Germany, Canada and the USA. The Natura is appealing to folks wanting a relaxing get-away, families and the like. In other words, don't expect a huge party atmosphere.GROUNDS: The Park's grounds are lovely. They're nicely maintained and don't have that hyper-manicured look you'd expect at a super-high-end resort. Kids will enjoy seeing the flamingoes during the day and hearing the frogs at night in one of Natura's many ponds. The freshwater fish are fun to watch and feed from the pedestrian bridges.DINING: They offer a wide range of items in their breakfast, lunch and dinner offerings. Most everyone can find something they like. Picky eaters, food snobs and the like will most likely be underwhelmed: a culinary gem the Natura is not, so keep expectations in check.BEACH: Really nice. The white sand is super soft, the water is turquoise/blue, and the palm trees sway on cue. Little thatched shelters are plentiful, but get there mid-morning at the latest to secure one. The Natura is located at the end of a string of resorts, which means you can expect minimal foot traffic along the beach. This provided a sense of privacy definitely not available at nearby resorts. ROOMS: Comfortable and clean. The AC worked well, which came in handy when the temp soared to 95 degrees F in the afternoon. Our room got pretty muggy at times, which was to be expected given the tropical location.STAFF: Courteous and hard-working. Don't expect everyone there to speak fluent English. Tips are appreciated.I would stay at the Natura again in future visits.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good time had by all We just returned from the Natura having stayed June 28th-July 1. My husband and I went with my sister and her husband. We have stayed at several all inclusives and this one ranked right up there with the others. The grounds are beautiful and the ground keepers work very hard to maintain it. One was cutting down some fruit from a tree, I am assuming so it would not fall on someone walking by and offered it to me. The flamingos are beautiful and it was fun to see the geese laying on their eggs. The peacock was fun especially when it came right up to our table at the main buffet. The rooms were pretty good. It does have a natural feel. It would have been nice to have a more private bathroom door. The maids were good and even came back and re-mopped our floor after the maintance men had to fix a leaking toilet. They put flowers on the bed each day. The pool was nice although we spent most of the time in the ocean. The swim up bar was fun. The bar above the swim up bar was a nice cool place to sit at night. Too bad the bartender, Francisco didn't work at night. He made the best banana mamas. The beach was great. We didn't have trouble finding a hut to sit under but if you want one right close to the water, you should go down early and reserve one. There was some sea grass floating but it wasn't slimy so it didn't really bother us. Plus, you are in the ocean so things will be floating from time to time. I felt so sorry for the worker who had to sweep it each day, put it in a wheel barrel and wheel it down the beach to where he dumped it for a truck to pick it up. And we all complain about our jobs!!!!! We went snorkeling to the left of the beach when you are looking at the water. There is a tree fallen down and there are two good locations. The better of the two, which is farther out is not real safe as it is outside the protected swim area and you have to watch out for speed boats coming by. There is also an area right outside the rope in the swim area that was nice. Make sure you take bread with you and your underwater camera. We took rafts to float out in the ocean and I would highly recommend doing that. Talk about relaxing. We bought cheap ones and then left them there instead of deflating. There are shops down the beach, but we found them not to be real cheap as in someother countries we have been to. You can deal with them, but it takes persistence on your part. I don't know if it is the same day each week, but Thursday night, they were up by the main buffet. Now about the food. It was pretty good, nothing great though. We definitely did not go hungry though. There is the main buffet which is where we had breakfast. Then there is the steak house, which we ate at and it was good. We did not eat at the Italian. My sister and brother in law ate at the seafood one night and said it was good. We usually ate lunch at the buffet by the pool as you could just walk in with your suits on and it had a beautiful view of the ocean. We noticed that men without long pants were eating in the steakhouse and the main buffet at night although we were told that you were supposed to wear long pants. So we tried it one night and didn't have any problems. There isn't much night life but that was ok since we were there with another couple. Not many people spoke English as a first language but we didn't have any trouble in terms of a language barrier. Now for a couple negatives, it rained briefly one night right before we ate dinner at the steakhouse by the pond. Just as we were finishing our meals, the mosquitos decided it was time for them to eat. But the staff was right there with bug spray although we still encountered many bites. So bring bug spray and be proactive and spray it on before you eat. You have to call for the mini fridge to be unlocked after you arrive and they lock it the day before you leave. But they did come get out the free stuff when we called and asked them to open it back up. So we got the sodas and the beers for the night, but they weren't cold. It would be nice if the fridge was just stocked with the freebies and then you wouldn't have that hassel. Also the electricity went off a couple times, but for 5-10 minutes tops. I still wished I had brought a flashlight. Also, there are no clocks so you might want to bring one. It didn't really bother us that much, since we weren't concerned with time. We did pay the $50.00 for a late check out since our shuttle to the airport wasn't coming until 7:00 for our 10:20 flight. There is a small locker room that you can shower in but when we went to check it out, it was hot and the luggage area was not secured by a staff person. As mentioned in other reviews, the is a switch that you have to keep something inserted into in order to keep your electricity on. When we got to our room, it was already going. Someone had stuck a brochure in it. So we didn't have any problems with that. It was slightly a pain to have to worry about the key to the safe. I like the code safes better, but I just took an extra key ring and put it on there or you could attach it to your room key. We felt safe leaving our things on the beach unattended but remember that your room key does have your room number on it so one could access your room and your safe if it was lost or stolen. Overall, for the price we paid for the trip (we did get a really good deal), we thought the resort was great. We didn't venture off the resort so I cannot comment on anything off the resort. We would good back to Punta Cana and would consider going back to the resort when we have seen the other places we want to go to or if we get another great deal. Try it, you'll like it.

<Author>Ashanti137
<Content>Spectacular! Natura Park is a slice of heaven. The grounds with all of its vegetation and wildlife are spectacular. There are all kinds of beautiful birds, peacock, flamingos, varieties of ducks and fish. The resort is very well maintained.Despite language differences, the staff was very helpful, friendly, and accomodating. In particular, the activities staff members are young, professional, energetic, and sincerely dedicated to helping guests get involved and have fun. We participated in many of the beach games, getting to know numerous guests from all over. Our room was quite spacious with a walk-in closet. The room had the usual iron and board, blow-dryer, stocked mini-bar, coffee-maker, and safe. There was a large balcony overlooking a small lake. The lay-out of the room maximized privacy with the inclusion of a small foyer-like entry area from which the bedroom and bathroom areas were not visible. The main dining area, La Cana, was conveniently located. There was a very wide variety of dishes and many different specialty centers for things like fresh-made fresh-fruit smoothies, omelettes, pasta dishes, breads desserts, and coffees. The hostesses and waiters, especially Miguel, were exceptional in their hospitality and service. The executive chef was also very personalble and genuinely concerned about the guests' satisfaction and enjoyment of not only the meals, but thewhole Natura Park experience. We were able to get a reservation, with some difficulty, in the seafood restaurant, La Perla. The grilled lobster and wine were very, very good. The Spa at Natura Park is very nice. My fiance and I had massages and we were both very pleased. The prices were very good ($65 for 55 minutes). There's also a sauna, steamroom, exercise facility, and hair salon within the spa.Despite very full days, we managed to muster up the energy to go to the evening shows on the premise. Great band and excellent dancers and choreography! Each night had a different theme and different activities. One night there was a dance contest in which the audience voted by applause to select a winner among four couples. The ceiling fans in the area where the shows were could have been on much higher as the room was quite warm. One suggestion that we wish we'd remembered was to carry our own large thermal-type containers to keep soemthing cold to drink nearby! The plastic cups were very small and the ice melted immediately!We took an excursion booked through a third-party agent. I would strongly recommend going directly through a tour agent such as CoCo Tours. At first we were told by the agent at Connect Travel Services that the tour (to Sonoa Island) was full and we would have to reschedule. However, since we were leaving the next day, we insisted on keeping the reservation for the day for which we were supposedly confirmed for. The Connect Travel agent agreed and scheduled us for pick-up on the morning of the original reservation date. The Connect Travel bus arrived actually early that morning. We had a rather short ride to another location where we were to meet up with the rest of the tour party. We waited for over an hour and a half at a restaurant in nearby Higuley. Once the other bus arrived, we had a rather long, but scenic and interesting drive to the port. Overall, the excursion was loads of fun and well worth the cost.I would highly recommend Natura Park to those who love beautiful natural surroundings and want a wide variety of on-site activiities, including plain old RR! After a couple of brief visits to other hotels in the area, we were very glad we'd chosen Natura Park. And when it was time to leave, the sadness we felt as we said our goodbyes to new friends, assured us that we had discovered a very special place with very special people.

<Author>Searchin 4 Sun
<Content>A great time at a great price My wife and I came with no preconceived notions since we ended up at Natura Park on a 4 Apple Square Deal from May 12th to the 19th. All in all, the positives far outweigh the negatives. The beach is beautiful and relaxing and the pool and the lunch buffet are just a few steps away. The grounds are also beautiful. Our room was fine except for a drip from the air conditioner.The staff is very friendly, particulularly when you consider that they work 12-14 hours a day for 11 days in a row, before getting 3 days off. Many of the ones we got to know told us that their families lived hours away and they only got to see them on their three day weekend. They greatly appreciate and need any small tip you can give them. Since my wife speaks fluent Spanish (mine is ok) we were able to communicate with no problem but I can see how it might be difficult for someone who doesn't speak any Spanish. The drinks were of decent quality for an all-inclusive and they carried name brands such as Stoly, Tanquarey and Johnny Walker. The food was medicore at best but we didn't go there to eat.For shopping there are little shacks down the beach. We recommend Papito in store # 13.Perhaps our biggest complaint was a lack of late night activity as not much goes on after 11:30. This, however, turned into a positive when we organized midnight taxi trips to the Mangu disco which is about 20 minutes away. ($24 each way split between 8 people). We met a lot of interesting people at Natura Park from Europe and from the U.S. and our trips to the disco were great bonding experiences. So if you have an open mind and are a little adventuresome there is some late night fun to be had.I would advise folks to bring a lot of small US bills for tips, shopping and incidentals. It is can be very difficult to get money since the ATMs right off the grounds rarely have money in them. If you are able to get money out of the ATM (Dominican of course) it is even more difficult to get it converted into dollars.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We had an amazing vacation! My husband and I just returned from a wonderfully relaxing holiday at Natura Park. Thanks to the mixed reviews for the resort, we weren't sure what to expect. However, we found the staff to be incredibly friendly and accomodating, the food to be great and plentiful (especially the wonderful juice bar at breakfast), the grounds, pool, and beach to be BEAUTIFUL, and our air-conditioned room to be fantastic (and not at ALL run down). We loved the open-air structure of the main building, which contains the buffet restaurant, performance stage, a bar, a game room, an internet access room, the gift shop and reception. I especially enjoyed passing by flamingos, ducks, peacocks, and geese (which were nesting!) during every walk through the grounds.  I know some people were upset that your key needs to be inserted into a slot on the wall of the room for the lights to work, but that is simply because Natura Park is an Eco Resort that is making a very welcome effort to save energy. One of the helpful resort staff walked us to our room after we checked in and showed us how it worked. My husband and I were extremely pleased to note the many efforts that the management is making to conserve energy and resources while still accomodating guests to an extremely high quality! Personally, I don't know why people would want to keep the lights on in their room while they are not in it anyway. My husband and I were at the resort for six days and could easily have spent another week there. We didn't even partake in all of the free activities that were available (such as paddle boating, a SCUBA lesson in the pool, and wind surfing) because we were so occupied with other activies...as well as simply relaxing!! We did go kayaking and snorkeling, played tennis every day, went on a fantastic excursion during which we were able to drive speed boats and snorkel at a beautiful nearby coral reef, attended the evening entertainment (performed by resort staff with incredible dancing talent and great senses of humor), and enjoyed the pool bar :)We are not wealthy people and do not have the funds to go to a so-called five star resort, but I certainly don't understand why Natura Park is not rated higher than it is. My husband and I would return in a heartbeat. My one piece of advice is to bring a large supply of sunblock because it is very expensive in the gift shop - between $14 to $27 per bottle. We had to buy some when ours ran out. Otherwise, we had a perfect experience and we highly recommend this resort to anyone who wants to relax in a gorgeous location surrounded by travelers from around the world and the most friendly resort staff I have ever had the pleasure of knowing.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>an agents view My husband and I are both travel agents and returned recently from the Natura Resort, Punta Cana. So I will give you some hints and tell you what the rest seem to leave out. Yes the grounds are as lovely as all the reviews say, the pool is a good size and yes it is not heated. There are very few heated pool in the Caribbean or Mexico, the sun does it naturally and with the hot temps a cool pool is refreshing most days.ROOMS; were large, the bed very firm, but surprisingly comfortable. A huge walkin closet, bring extra hangers there were 8. We opened the balcony doors for a while and the room aired out. RESTAURANTS; the buffet is ok Breakfast is the best of the three meals, lunch and dinner are so so. There are lots of choices but it would rate the least favourite of all the inclusive resorts we have stayed at. The specialty restaurants are wonderful. The first day you are there go to the customer service desk in the lobby 9am -1pm and 4pm-8pm and they will book all three restaurants, give you slips with confimations and times and you are set for the week. I suggest booking early times to eat, some of the popular entrees run out later.If you try to do this on a daily basis you will never get in.This is a Spanish owned hotel that is a favourite of Europeans. You will find that there will be no facetowels in the rooms on arrival. Bring some from home and as soon as you meet your maid she will provide faceclothes and extra towels. Europeans do not use facetowels nomally. We had no problem once our maid knew we were from Canada.Because so many guests are from Europe be prepared for smokers, everywhere. In the pools(with cups for ashes) on the beach, in the restaurants, shows. The European women also like to go topless. On the beach, at the pool, the beach bar, swimup bar etc.STAFF; we had no problem with english at the desk, customer service and most restaurants. Very little english is spoken at the bars and we had a few with waiters.The maids do not speak english.Bring a clock there aren't any in the rooms and wake-up calls are not reliable. The resort was fine. We enjoyed good swimming and an nice beach. Would we go back to the Dominican, no never. There was a a feeling of never being really safe, and we were very aware that the Europeans are the perfered guests.

<Content>Would go back in a heart beat! I returned from this resort a few days ago, and I did not want to leave. The rooms were soooo clean that when we moved the beds around, there wasn't even a ball of dust to be seen underneath them.The resort beach area was acceptable, but take a walk to the left and you will find the most beautiful beach. It was truely picturesque. No sea weed, no crowds. It was breath taking.My complaints:1. They offer motorized water sports, and I felt that there were many boats going by relatively close to the swimming area, mostly like to avoid the reef.2. Stack up on 1$ bills for tips and try to avoid having to withdraw money at the resort as it is a small walk outside the grounds to an ATM machine with only dominican pesos (obviously). The staff also appreciated commodities like tooth paste or perfum as an alternative to money, so bring those old perfums you don't use that your great aunt gave you.
