<Content>Loved it! If you would like a serene, calm and restorative experience, the Natura Park is for you! We have traveled to many islands and this was the best run resort we have been at. Everything ran smoothly, on-time, and most importantly- anytime you had a question, they answered it easily and quickly. We were a few of the only Americans there- mostly Germans and eastern Europeans. Lots of Domincans there for the weekend EAster holiday. Blau is a German resort company.ROOM- Clean, comfortable, not as fancy as some hotels, but nice. We didn't think the beds were wonderful, but we slept well each night. MAID SERVICE- Following a previous traveler's tip, we left a little gift each day for our maid and asked for anything we needed. She was a doll and went out of her way to help us. She was very appreciative of our gifts. (Her name was Nedia)LOBBY, BARS- Beautiful! Helpful people, comfortable. There is a large giftshop, medical cneter, restrooms, help desk, registration.ENTERTAINMENT-They have a wonderful house jazz band with a fantastic trumpet player. For the later evening there is a resident dance troupe that puts on great shows. What energy! Don't miss the From the Movies show- it is wonderful!!!!!BEACH- We loved it. We like to snorkel and there are wonderful things to see right off the beach. There is a little seaweed, but they keep it very well raked up. The pristine beaches have no fish!!! MAny, many people were snorkeling all week.GROUNDS- Different from any other resort. They have received awards for their ecological management. The buildings are no higher than 3 stories and use a lot of natural materials. The grounds are full of beautiful (labeled for you gardeners!) plants and ponds full of fish, egrets and other fishing birds. there are pairs of geese and ducks everywhere and peacocks. Very entertaining.FOOD- If you can't find something to eat here, you are way too fussy. From our experience, sticking to native specialities is always a good idea and sure enough the chicken, rice and bean dishes were great, but there were roasts, steaks, pork chops and a million salads, veggies, stir-fires and paellas. There is afternoon tea and pastries in the lobby bar each afternoon. Don't miss the whipped cream cakes! The coffee is amazing.TRIPS- We took the Caribbean Fest snorkeling trip- go for the dancers on board, but not for the snorkeling! Too crowded!!!We also took the cave trip to Los Haitises What an adventure!!!!! Not for the faint of heart (or legs) but a trip I will never forget. AFter a 2 1/2 hour ride, we arrived at our site and hiked for 45 minutes (rugged hike) then went on horseback for 1/ 2 hour. We had a light breakfast at the ranch and donned canvas overalls and rubber boots (you can't take anything else with you at this point) At the mouth of the cave you are put in a mountaineering harness and lowered 60 ft into a cave. It is a 2 hour trip to 120 feet underground with amazing formations and a swim in an underground river. The guide helped me since I am not a swimmer. It was AWESOME and worth every penney. The guide is Jaoni (sp?) and he is great and entertaining.The airport is wretched- very unfriendly and confusing. Check you are in the right place, We almost missed our flight and I found out afterwards that also happened to friends later in the week.So try NATURA PARK- you won't be sorry!LB from Stockton, NY

We kept our valuables in the safe which uses a key not a code, so if your shorts are stolen on the beach they have your room key with your room number on it and your safe key.On the evening of the third day I went to open my son's room with my room key and he said,  How did you open the door with the security lock on? <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful Beach If you are planning to go to Punta Cana, Dominican Rep., I can recommend the beautiful resort, Natura Park Eco Resort. In this resort, you can find a beautiful natural environment, wild birds , very quiet and clean rooms, great and friendly people (even though not all staff speak English, however, all of them are willing to make your vacation enjoyable). The beach is beautiful with white sand and you can walk forever. There are no vendors harassing guests on the beach. The water is clear and the beach is well maintained with plenty of lounge chairs. There were the usual resort activities: volleyball, water polo, some meringue lessons.On the other hand, in our experience there are many things that the management could improve and make this a 5 star Resort. For example: If you like alcoholic beverages be prepared to drink a lot because in my opinion the bottles are diluted with something, but I am not sure. Some wine was poured from a large white plastic bleach container!If you purchased all inclusive package you have the right to have a la carte dinners in each of the 3 restaurants, my advice; if you drink wine (red or white) purchase your own at the Duty Free because the Spanish house wine that they serve with the meals is terrible! The food was better than the buffet, but in this resort, food and drink is not the highlight.Talking about the buffet, in my personal opinion, in general its ok. Some of the meals in the buffet were very greasy, and very salty, and the seafood is not great as I expected. We were a little sick after eating seafood but we are not sure if the seafood was the cause. However, be prepared and take a big bottle of Pepto Bismol with you (helps). Another good piece of advice is; bring small bills in American dollars because it is very difficult to change large bills for small ones. Tip your room maid the first day and you will get plenty of water, coffee, beer extra towels and changed linens when you want. There is a spa on site, (extra charge) the mud massage (called fango) was great. 3 clay tennis available. After spending a week in Natura Park, I found our time was enjoyable, we had a good time in a beautiful place, and people were very hospitable. However, I won鈥檛 come back there, I will try another resort in the Caribbean next time.

We all found our rooms and the ones that requested king beds got them and the others were happy with there oversized twins beds. It was windy at times and the weeds did build up but were no problem and didn't interfer with swimming. The pool was nice and clean and really refreshing, the waterfall to get up to the bar was a little challenging but fun.The drinks were always good and never had a problem with service at the bars. The hotel has many bridges and ponds where people could feed the fish, ducks, geese, turtles, and whatever else flew over for a bite.The food at the buffet was really good and you could always find something to eat. We ate at the Seafood resturant and had lobster and fish and its was very good.We also ate at the Steakhouse, the food there was exceptly good and the service was awesome. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved It, but beware My wife and I spent one glorious week at the Natura Park Resort from March 4 - 11, 2006. On the whole the resort was fantastic. The grounds are stunning, the facilities are above average and the beach is perfect (some seaweed, but it is not a problem). Alot of wildlife wander the grounds. We met Bossy Boots and the wife(ducks) who absolutely have control over the grounds. They are no problem whatsover, and provide alot of fun. ROOMS: The rooms are average sized and are kept very clean. The cleaning staff ensured the rooms were cleaned and the sheets were changed regularly. We always had hot water and towels; our request for extra toilet paper was answered quickly! The shower would leak when used but again it was no problem.FOOD: We would have to say the food was average, the buffet may have been a little boring as far as selection goes. The steakhouse was by far the best a la carte restaurant, followed by the Italian restaurant, we did not eat in the Seafood restaurant but heard from other guests it was okay. We would liked to have seen more snacks available during the day. Unfortunately we were both sick one day. Don;t forget to take the Immodium. FACILITIES: The pool and beach were perfect, the swim up bar saw a lot of action! The pool was extremely clean and the water was refreshing. People have said they found it cold, we did not. The beach was great. The water was very warm, just perfect. Some seaweed would wash up, as expected, but there was always a crew on duty to clean it up. The drinks are in no way watered down you are always served with a smile. Highly recommended, the Blau's. Lots of activities are planned daily, the crazy games are fun , the beer chugging contest always will provide a laugh. The staff in charge of the activities were absolutely wonderful and they also included the children.(childrens) The 10:00 am call was Wakey Wakey for the stretching. These people were stil there at 10:00 pm. at night.(They worked very hard).WEATHER: Perfect, one day of clouds, there is always a wind blowing. From our experience mornings tend to be cloudy, but the clouds did retreat by mid-morning.STAFF: Generally the staff were terrific. The waiters, bartenders, cleaning staff, and hostesses were more than friendly and always willing to help you to ensure you are comfortable. These people were always grateful for any tips, which they deserved! However please be aware that the staff you wish to be the most helpful and friendly, namely the reception staff, guest services staff and our tour operator were the least helpful of all! We experienced problems in securing our reservations for the a la carte restaurants (for some reason we were always asked to come back at a later time, and when we did so were told no reservations were available, then when pushed a reservation for a later time was opened). The reception staff did not seem interested in providing assistance. We were running low on money, we were told that an ATM was just off-site of the grounds. We discovered however the ATM was out of service and had been for the previous couple of days and the staff was aware of this, yet still were directing guests to use it. After much discussion we were advised there was a bank located at a neighboring resort approximately 5 minutes away by cab. We asked reception staff to call us a cab repeatedly. After 45 minutes of waiting it was clear that none of the staff saw to our request. By chance our tour operator from Sunwing happened by and when he was told of our predicament he showed no interest in helping us nor did he provide us with any assistance other than calling us a cab and asking us If we were happy now? The tour operator also directed us to the ATM but when we advised him it was not in service he acknowledged that he knew that but did not offer any explanation as to why he would send us back there knowing it was not in service. Please be aware that if you need to go to a bank make sure you have your passport with you. ATM's dispense only pesos. This was another bit of info that was not relayed to us which they were aware of . We spent $10.00 on a cab , got to the bank and they would not help us without a passport. Also be aware that if you have a late flight out of the country the resort will give you an option of retaining your room beyond the noon hour checkout(if available)for an additional fee of $25.00 U.S. per person. We decided to take advantage of this and were told we could retain our room until 4:30 the day of our checkout, but what was not told to us prior was that payment was cash only!We discovered this when we were checking out not having sufficient U.S. funds left they would not accept payment for this charge on our credit card. After much discussion and asking to speak with management, they finally accepted the credit card but they were not happy to do so. The hotel did give you a complimentary room for showers and luggage storage but there was a lineup of about 5 people at one time wanting to use the facilities about an hour before the bus was picking us up. OVERALL: Overall we have to say our stay was enjoyable. Although frustrating the problems encountered did not damper our vacation too much. This was our first time to the Dominican having travelled in Mexico previously there is a discernable difference between the 2 countries. We will know better next time if we decide to return to the DR. We met some very fantastic people that only added to our enjoyment. We would like to say hi to Rich  Dianne from New Jersey, Ryan  Shannon from Montreal, and Bambi and the gang from Pittsburgh if any of you are reading this we would love to keep in touch and our e-mail address is engler79@sympatico.ca. One bit of advice if we may to the European travellers, staff at the resort are not your personal valets or your personal staff. Treat them with some respect, a smile can go a long way. In concluding I am sure everyone will enjoy their stay at this resort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Didn't want to leave We just returned from Natura Park resort yesterday. We had beautiful weather every day and a really good time. It was very windy a couple of the days on the beach, but never a problem and up at the pool area, you barely noticed wind at all. The grounds are beautiful, you can get a lot of great photos. Birds, ducks, beautiful flamingo's and peacocks roam freely on this resort. The gym is great and spa was very nice. Rooms are large and very clean. The resort was very busy, actually more people than we anticipated, but it is prime time for people to get away from winter. Just takes a day to settle in. The beach chairs are a problem, you have to reserve them early (before breakfast) or they're all gone and you end up spending your day laying on your towel. It's no fun wandering around trying to find a spot to sit on the beach, so if you want a chair, get up early. Seaweed was bad on the windy days, but raked up daily. There is lots of activity on this resort. The staff was always friendly and helpful. Food was ok. If you keep to the basics you'll be ok. Lots of food we would never eat, but we managed out ok. They make great omlettes and fruit smoothy's. We ate lunch at the beach resturaunt every day, pizza, fries, burger (weren't great) nacho's and an assortment of salads, pasta, fruit and desserts. We enjoyed our dinners in the specialty resturaunts, the Italian was good and the steakhouse was the best. The seafood ok. The buffet suppers were ok, but again lots of different foods that we don't like. You can't expect the food to be like it is a home. Don't over-indulge and don't mix drinks. Stick to what you're familiar with. The quality of liquor isn't the same as at home. We bought duty-free liquor, poured it into a pepsi bottle and took it in our beach bag every day and just got the pepsi from the bar. The lobby bar is the nicest, larger range of drinks but the beach bar is very nice at night. You can sit and listen to the ocean. We enjoyed this resort but it would have been perfect if there had been a relaxation pool. The main pool is very busy, but had an awesome swim-up bar with a waterfall and bubble pool. We would recommend this resort, just keep in mind, things are different in the Dominican, don't expect it to be perfect and relax.

<Content>great time Just returned from a great week at Natura Park Resort. The grounds were great and very well maintained. <Author>travel_guy_toronto
<Content>Loved it...       beach picture  
<Date>Feb 8, 2006
<Rating>4	4	5	-1	5	-1	4	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Most Reviews are correct. Your attitude determines outcome! Ok, it's going to be long and detailed...Let me start by saying, that this was our third trip to Dominican Republic, and the two previous trips were to far more elite and expensive resorts. None the less we enjoyed this particular vacation the most. This is not to say that the hotel was the best, it's just the attitude. First and foremost - we were well familiar with Dominican style by now, and knew very well what to expect. Most reviewers - good and bad, provide the correct information on this forum. The resulting conclusions and rating, IMO is just a result of their attitude towards it.Let me set an example of a wrong attitude right away: One morning I was in the buffet standing in lane for the omlettes. The chef did not speak any English to talk about (as many of the staff), but made great omlettes and fried eggs, a few hand gestures and sometimes spanish words you could find in most phrase books did the trick. Before me was a couple of cocky Americans. They showed chef the eggs and said two over easies!. He put eggs on the grill. Then when they were almost ready chef asked them by gesture if they wanted the eggs flipped. Their response: Comon, everyone knows what over easy is!. No hand gesture, just these words and look of disappointment on their faces. If this is your attitude - you may want to choose a different hotel, or even a different country, where English is widely spoken and service is more like in the States.Now to the details - I'll try to go through things I read in this forum prior to visiting the hotel and give a more or less objective evaluation to them.1. Language:As I mentioned in example above, if you live in the world where English is the only language, and you expect that it'll be spoken in every corner of the world you visit, and you feel insulted when not understood in plain and simple English - choose a different hotel, and even better a different country. After all, when people from Spain visit the United States, they don't get insulted that YOU don't speak Spanish, do they? Ok, English is very little there. VERY. Remember, that Blau, the company that manages this hotel is Spanish, and most tourists are non English-Speaking. So English is not requirement for most jobs in this resort. Not even on Front Desk everyone speaks English, though there at front desk and in a la carte restaurants everyone knows how to say basic things related to their duties. We never had much trouble getting the point across. The staff is very nice and appreciative, especially when they see you try to communicate with them using the 5-6 words you know in Spanish. 2. Dominican Minute:This is an ongoing joke I've heard in all three visits to DR. The people there are slow. SLOW. If someone tells you they'll be there in 5 minutes - don't expect them in 5 minutes. It's Dominican minutes, and one Dominican minute may last up to regular 10 minutes or more. They know it, and they joke about it all the time. If you are not getting what you want, ask again! Yes, we had to ask at the front desk and make 2 phone calls to have our minibar unlocked on the first day of our trip. So that's how Dominicans are. If you want things done fast - go to New York!3. Staff, tipping, etc: People there are friendly. If you are friendly to them. We never yelled or demanded things from people, and they always responded kindly. A little tip here and there is always appreciated, though nobody expects you to tip (a couple of times I had to almost chase down the waitress to give tip). However - don't expect that if you tip, you'll get a VIP treatment right away. May happen, may not. We tipped staff occasionly, always tipped the maid (and left her little gifts we brought along from a 99 cent store). There were always smiles, and sometimes some extras. When we were just checking in, I immediately tipped the receptionist, winked and asked that he get us a good room. Don't know what would've happen otherwise, but our room had no problems people were talking about in other reviews. 4. Other tourists: Most people in the resort were there to enjoy their vacations. Again, the majority were not Americans. Lots of people from Spain, Italy, Germany, Netherlands, Austria, Russia, etc. Also folks from South America. I've personally seen more Canadians than Americans during our trip. What I didn't see were rude europeans as some reviewers describe them. Of course there may be one or two individuals that wre not nice. But I won't generalize. Let me stress once again - if you are not willing to accept that there are cultures other than American, you may want to visit an all-American resort or stay in the States. Maybe this is because we ourselves were born in Eastern Europe and immigrated to the States as teenagers we had a better time being around this crowd. But if you simply don't understand their language - it doesn't mean they're bad. And during the nightly shows, when audience participation was required - thanks to those Europeans they were really fun! There was at least one large group of Spanish students that we saw on a few occasions. No problems with them. They may have made a little noise, but nothing to complain about. This is a resort - a place where people relax. If you don't like somebody, just step away from them. To conclude the topic - we actually enjoyed being among the crowd that's nothing like what we see every day at home. It's different, it's fun and it's relaxing. Loosen your breaks and enjoy the stay.5. Territory: I think this is the only topic on which most reviewers before me agreed. The territory is absolutely beautiful and well kept. 6. Mosquitos: Do bring some mosquito repellant. You may need it - or you may not. There is a lot of standing water on the territory, so naturally there are mosquitos. However, we only had one close encounter with little beasts. When we dined in the Steakhouse a la carte restaurant (Media Luna), which is positioned right over the artificial pond - the little creatures had their own fest on us. Stepping just a few yards away, and there were none. No mosquitos to be found in our room (we kept the screen door closed on the patio) or other restaurants, lobby, etc. If you live in one of the patios that's directly above water - it may be a bigger problem though, I can't testify to that...7. Beach: This is not the best piece of beach to be found in DR. However it has some advantages, and really big ones. Firstly, the sea weed was somewhat a problem, though not big enough to spoil the vacation. There was plenty washed out to the shore. Hotel staff kept working on removing it all day long. Also some ween in the sea. The sea, however, was clear enough to see where the weed spots are and they could be easily avoided when going in the water. But here's the good part - about half a mile into the sea there's a massive coral reef running right across the beach. It provides excellent protection against the rough sea. First few days of our vacation were very windy (20 miles per hour according to forecasts I've seen before departing). But our sea was calm! Just small waves, nothing to be worrying about. We could see huge waves breaking up against the reef far in the sea. None reached us! This is great compared to our previous trips to hotels farther north. No reef there, and in windy weather it was quite a showtime in the sea! Now, here's another thing about beach. This resort is last in the line, and from there a few miles of uninhibited beach stretch northward. Some of the places on that beach were nicer than at hotel. So many people took advantage by visiting them or even bringing their towels and spending all day there! If you want to go for a long walk on that beach - bring a footwear. At certain point (and we walked as far as next chain of hotels) beach becomes some sort of clay and rocks, and you may want to take the footpath in the forest, 15 feet from the beach. But you want to wear something on your feet there, simple flip-flops will do.8. Accomodations:As mentioned above - don't know if the initial $5 tip made it that way, but I would rate our room 5 out of 5. Clean, well maintained, no mossy smell or mold to be found. We were on the second floor of the three floors in patio II. The room was surprisingly big. Not a typical hotel room. Furniture - not many, a king bed (request one in advance, per their web site limited king bed rooms are available), a desk, couple of chairs, and that's it. Walk-in closet was a nice touch. It didn't have much shelves to put stuff on, however there was a big bench on which we settled our suitecases and used them as the makeshift closet. Shower, bathroom - no problems to report. The bathtub form prompted some water to end up on the floor when we showered, that's probably the only problem. A quick wipe with the towel solved it for us. Our room was not far from the lobby, and yes, we could hear very well the music from the nightly enterntainment/disco. Especially when veranda door was open, which we liked to do instead of AC. It ran pretty late (till 1.30am, I think), so if it bothers you - request a room closer to the beach. We slept very well to the sound of merengue though ;-)9. Food:If eating gourmet meals is the purpose of your trip - skip this resort. We always found something to eat, but food is definetly not the selling point for this place. For breakfest - omlettes were great, a good choice of European style meets and cheeses available as well. No American style continental breakfest. Scrambled egg looked a little scarry, but we were not funs of that anyway. For lunch we liked the beach buffet better. Chicken was always good. Burgers on the beach not very attractive. Dinner - a la carte food wasn't bad. I've ate a better lobster (I won't rate it bad either - just not very remarkable), but the Italian and Steakhouse were pretty good. Service was excellent in a la carte (except, maybe, steakhouse). Waiters stood by waiting for a first sign that you need them, just like in the most expensive restaurants I've been to. Dinner buffet - not bad. Every night there was a different theme - Japanses, Dominican, Italian, etc., with different dishes served. Plus the standard collection of dishes available every night. If nothing else appealed - pasta was always there to enjoy. Food temperature: Ok, this is a painful topic to many. Let's set it straight - all restaurants are open air. Food cools down very quickly, even if standing on heaters all the time. I made an interesting observation: One morning I picked up two pieces of boiled ham in the breakfest buffet, while waiting for my omlette to be done. I was very hungry, so I just ate one right away, and it was comfortably warm (warm enough for enjoyment, but not too hot to keep on cooking). Then I picked up my omlette, a glass of orange juice and settled at the table. When I bit on the second piece, it was cold. So, things get cold there quickly. Hard to keep them hot. The lunch chicken in beach buffet was always hot, because we ate during the peak time, and it went very fast. They kept cooking and putting out new trays. So no problem there. But if it's been out for 15 minutes, even on heater, don't expect to eat it hot. Once again - if you go there for food, you'll be disappointed, as with several exceptions the general food quality was medium.10: Drinks:In Lobby bars drinks were generally better than on the beach. They don't use things like shakers or blenders at all. Just mix drinks in the glass and use crushed ice from the machines for frozen drinks. Other than that - drinks were decent. Definetly not a five-star bar service, but I found them acceptable. Surprisingly, in the bars the service was quick, given the number of people making orders. I guess not using shakers/blenders helped to speed things up, but I've never had to wait for more than a minute before somebody took my order and never more than another minute or two before it was completed. Provided a number of people around the bar at all times and the dominican minute concept described above - I think this is a great speed!11: Activities/spa/etc.:When the wind settled there was a run of things you could do on the beach for free: kayaking, katamarans, etc., but you had to reserve those in advance. Also a good selection of motorized sports. We went to Parasailing and loved it. Reserved and paid for right through hotel - not through guys sitting in their speedboats between hotels as it often happens. Spa was good - my wife really enjoyed the package she got there. And the prices were right. I thought they were pretty cheap for a resort! Jacuzzi not included. At first we were disappointed, but then we realized something else. You have to make a reservation to use it. However when we came for the first time not knowing that, they just looked that it's not reserved right now and made us a reservation for right now. Soecond for a small fee of just $5 per person we had jacuzzy for ourselves. No need to squeeze yourself between 12 pepole you've never met, as I've seen it in other resorts. We didn't book any outside excursions, but I don't think they are different than in other hotels. These are usually operated by same companies that contract hotels and they just pick you up wherever you stay.12: Entertainment:I'll rate it in the middle of the scale. During the day animation team ran some games on the beach and poolside. We are not funs of these activities, so can't comment on these, except that they seemed to always be there busy with something. Nightly shows: main complaint - they started too late. There was occasional kids show or just live music at 8pm, but the main show didn't start until 10pm. Good side is that you can have both the dinner and the show, but not wake up early next morning!. The shows themselves: Ones that were dancing and theatrical we found somewhat boring. Ok, we come from New York, the home of Broadway, and such, so we may be spoiled. But I'll still have to give them a medium to low mark. The interactive shows on the contrary were quite fun. In big part because the audience was very active and willing to participate and fool around a great deal. Of course nobody was required to participate. We just sat back there and watched the fun while enjoyed our drinks supplied from the bar by a friendly waitress. Secondly, I think the host of these shows did a great job. Speaking in 4 or 5 languages for everybody to understand he made them real enjoyable things to watch. Disco started after the main show, at 11:15-11:30 or so. Mostly latin music - merengue and such. Also some dancing could be done between the 8pm and 10pm shows, when animation folks often invited lonely members of the audience for a dance or two.13. Shopping:Hotel stores - pathetic. Two times during week local vendors came to the hotel with their craft. Haggle hard and you'll get a great deal! Finally, just 5-10 minutes walk down the beach to the south there's a small marketplace right on the beach. The vendors there are a bit pushy, but we got the best deals there, not in the hotel. Haggle. That's the main point. Go through all stalls, find one that has all things you need, get them all out, and negotiate the price for the entire set. Just make sure you know how much YOU want to pay for it before starting to haggle. Never pay more than half of their initial offer, and sometimes you can get as low as 1/3 or even 1/4 of that. Overall conclusion:This was the best value for the money we ever spent on vacation. We stayed in some much more expensive resorts, that were almost twice the cost of Natura Park and I don't feel like they were twice as good. Maybe time and a half in some respects, and even worse in others. It is definetly not a five star resort, I think 3.5 stars is a fair overall raiting for it. But I didn't find it *bad*. Once again, we loved our vacation. Will we come back? Honestly - not likely. But the reason is: we are just the kind of people who like to travel to a different place every year regardless of whether we liked the previous stay or not. On the other hand I will recommend this resort to most people I know, except the ones who like all american service if they can get a good deal on it!

<Author>KateSW
<Content>Would not go again We stayed at the hotel from Jan 21 to 28th 2006. We are a middle aged married couple who have done lots of traveling to many places overseas. The welcome at the desk was fine but take my advise and do not fly in from Baltimore- they land at La Romana which is 1 1/2 hours away from Punta Cana and I was pretty tired after the freezing bumpy ride and frustrated not to be able to get out and be among the people!! Our room was very large and comfortable with plenty of hot water, towels, soap, and drinking water. We were across from the nightclub so got to hear the show each night without even leaving the room! I would recommend making your reservations for the specialty restaurants soon after arrival and space them through the week as the food in the buffet does get old fast. I found the temp of the foods fine but the taste was sometimes a little off as if the chef had never tasted an original of whatever dish he was cooking. Do not miss Dominican night as the food was really superb that night. We did not have the best weather, not warm enough to swim and lots of wind on the beach. There is a problem with getting a chair poolside- they are all reserved fairly early in the am but there are plenty out on the lovely white sand beach. We were on an Apple vacation so all booze was covered (except from minibar) and the drinks were nice. This resort is out of the town so plan to spend about 38 US$ to get to town or just decide to stay put and enjoy a lazy stay. We did do the Crocodile dundee tour- mostly as a way to get out and see the countryside- it is stunningly beautiful and if you want to drink all day long this is the tour for you. They do have lovely grounds with lots of different birds and fish to look at and feed the leftover bread. My major problem is that I got an intestinal infection and I ate only what the resort provided the 24 hours prior to onset- my plane ride home was one I do not ever want to repeat. I believe I got the infection from chicken served at the taco bar so if you go eat only the grilled chicken and not the chopped up stuff they put out for nachos. A final word about dress- they ask for gentlemen to wear closed shoes and long pants at dinner especially in specialty restaurants but this was flagrantly ignored wear what makes you happy. I would not return to this resort as the food got tiresome and I prefer a little more local color and flavor in my travel.(Like camping under the stars with lions roaring all around me)

<Author>audiogal
<Content>A a good Time for a good price My husband and I stayed at Natura Park from 1/22-1/29/06. We paid a total of $900 per person from New York. We spoke to people from Canada, and even New Jersey, who paid less. For that price I think the resort was just fine. The grounds are lovely. The rooms were clean, though the bathrooms are a bit dated, with air conditioning that worked and a comfortable bed. Bring your own hair dryer. Afew times we did not have enough hot water. I got one bug bite all week. The beach is lovely. Yes there's some seaweed but it is cleaned several times per day. Get there early for a choice seat. The pool is a bit small for the size of the resort. The Punta Cana Princess has half the rooms and a bigger pool. We are beach people and only sat by the pool on the windiest of days. The staff could not be nicer. If you speak a little bit of Spanish it will go far. Learn to say hello (hola), please ( por favor), thank you (gracias) as it is common courtesy and much appreciated. There are many Europeans at the resort. I find them rude in a quiet way. They will reach over you to get food or a drink as if you're not there. They do not make eye contact if you speak. Europeans do not tip. I believe in Europe the tip is included so tipping is not their custom. This is a poor country and tipping is very much appreciated. I thought the food here was better than at the Punta Cana Princess (which cost more). Of course that's not saying much since the food is mediocre at best at these types of places. If you want a great meal go to New York, Chicago, L.A., Miami, Boston etc. not here. The food in Mexico is just a touch better. There was always something to eat here. The temperature of the food, hot or cold, would not pass the inspection of the department of health anywhere in the US. One night they had fresh pork that was tasty. Pasta was OK but ask them to cook it more (mas) to have it hotter. The buffet by the beach has rotisserie chicken every day at lunch which was usually fine. Once it was a bit overcooked, but I prefer that to undercooked! Rice and beans where good as was the salad and guacamole. We ate at the Italian restaurant. I had chicken and it was OK. My husband had steak and it was chewy and tasteless. The champagne was not bad and kept nicely chilled. Dinner at the steakhouse was better. The house band was really good and I would have liked to hear them play more. I only saw 10 nimutes of one of the 10pm shows and it was not worth staying up for. For the right price I would go back in a heartbeat. If you have any questions feel free to ask. mamie56@optonline.net

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Solo Traveller - Had a Fabulous Time at Natura Park Hello,I just came back from Natura Park. The grounds were fabulous!!! The pool was adequate, pretty, and deep enough for a good swim. My review is a bit long...It is interesting to hear different perspectives on this resort.I travelled alone as my husband was working and I wanted a pre-40th birthday treat.The negative reviews are surprising, but maybe my expectations were a little lower. We were in a third world country after all.Fellow travellers are right in saying that the staff's English was limited. Remember that in general, many Dominicans have not had the same opportunities as us. Problems were avoided because I made an effort to learn question words and some key verbs, and learned more vocabulary from the staff. Guest services were pretty good, especially Ximena, and Cindi. The staff were very helpful and kind to me, especially because I was alone and reached out to them, expressing gratitude in their language, albeit badly. ;-) I would like: QuisieroPlease; Por favorThank you; graciasA pleasure to meet you; mucho gustoGet a Spanish phrase book!!These politesses go a long way in making your stay much more pleasant. Treating the staff with kindness and respect will result in you being treated well in return. I think that more tourists need to learn this. I was appalled at how the staff were treated by some. I tipped occasionally, and the staff did not expect tips like in Cuba. I do wish that I brought things like notebooks, toothpaste, brushes, and other necessities for the people there.It was great meeting people from all over the world (Spain, Germany, France (love to practice my French),Belgium, the US... )and seeing the fun European fashions. The water was rather murky (but still turquoise) due to high winds and seaweed. The beach was really interesting as it is full of palm trees. The gentleman at the water sports centre told me that because we are in between rainy and dry season, the winds are a little higher and the weather is a bit turbulent. The clouds were pretty and the rain didn't bother me because it was warm. Unfortunately, they cancelled the 12$ snorkelling excursions due to the wind. I think it is a good deal. Windsurfing lessons were out of the question, too. I agree that it was frustrating to not get a seat on the beach or pool. A couple of times, after marked seats were vacant for a couple of hours, I just folded people's towels, placed them at the foot of the lounger, away from me, and sat on it. I had a copy of the multilingual hotel brochure in case I was challenged. No-one came back. ha haMy room was a little musty, but guest services helped with air fresheners and I loved my firm bed. I liked my room very much. The food was not too bad- lots of fruit, some veggies, good chicken, bad beef and lamb -mutton. ;-}The beach restaurant had good chicken and salsa.The buffet was not too bad. You can't go wrong with chicken!!Just south of the resort is hucksters' row ha ha. Cheapie cheapie, 99% off... Pay about 25% of what they ask. they can be agresssive. Be polite and they will be nicer.I enjoyed playing volleyball at the Occidental resort as well, just to the south of NP.North of the resort is a quieter beach which is interesting. I enjoyed our guided walk around the resort and on that beach.The Country Adventure tour was interesting and worth doing, but be prepared for a lot of time on the jeep thingie and a turbulent ride due to potholes. I was not feeling well that night and part of the next day due to the ride and the deisel fuel. Also, at the ranch it is wise to only eat the cooked food because you never know.. Bring hand sanitizer on these trips as well.I loved Natura Park because it wasn't a tacky party place. It had beautiful palapas and I think unpolished marble on the walls. The lobby is lovely and the sunsets are nice from there.The shows were fun (athletic dance routines - all 'round good fun). The animation team were lovely and I loved playing sports (v-ball, tennis, swimming, using the nice gym, and the merengue lessons. If you play tennis, make sure that you reserve and if you are a serious player, you may want to bring your own racquet. The racquets were adequate at best.There was a disco that lasted until just after one- a reasonable hour for an oldie like me. Overall, I give this holiday an 8.5 out of 10 (more than above average and less than excellent= 5 star at home. I had a fabulous, relaxing time and would consider bringing my husband back there. This resort is wonderful, and good value for the money paid.Cheers,Helen PS. bring insect repellant. The wretched bugs loved my skinny British ankles and wrists. I didn't feel them, until later. ;-0

The room had 2 single beds, so my husband and I snuggled in one bed. It was fine. The food was great! Lots of variety enough to please anyone. We went on a horseback riding tour and dinner both times we were there. It was incredible! I highly recommed it, we were treated extreamly well and the dinner we excellent! I recommend the sunset tour along the beach to the north of the resort. Keep track of your beach towel, you will be charged if you lose it. There is a market just down the beach. You will get the best deals if you buy everything from one vendor. Overall, it is a great resort and a bargin for a week in paradise.

<Author>mshklar
<Content>Paradise! My family just retuned from a week at Natura Park and had an absolutely wonderful vacation! The resort is gorgeous as might be expected given its focus on nature, but it exceeded all expectations. We booked our stay through Apple Vacations which used US Air. All flights and connections were on time. Airport transfers were perfect, and the check-in process was smooth. I had had some concerns based on the negative reviews on this site, and thought it might help other to explain the resort a bit.If you are lookeing for a high-energy vacation with lots of activites being organized for you, this is the wrong place to go. It is very low-key and relaxing (heavenly). Activities are certainly available.The resort is run by a Spanish company. Thus, the food bears a Spanish influence The breakfast buffet was very nice, lunches and the beach-side snack bar fine, and the dinner buffet very good. At the buffets it is best to concentrate on the fresh items (fruit, etc). and those which are featured. At all dinners there is a pasta bar and at brekfast an omlette station. The 3 specialty restaurants were very good, especially the seafood and the steak ones. Do not expect american-style food. Things like pasta dishes and pizza are a bit diffrent and very good.Rooms were exceptionally clean and certainly spacious for 2 people. No problems with utilities, etc. We were on the first floor (presumably the budget rooms) and had no noise issues.Staff were extremely kind and helpful, even though we do not speak Spanish. However, as an English-peaker you will be a minority here. If this makes you uncomfortable, you may not be happy although you can certainly take care of anything in Englsih with the resort staff. Waiters at all restaurants were very cheerful and helpful. Ditto housekeeping as all minor requests (exta water, bath towels etc) were attended to by leaving a note (using Berlitz' phrase book...)The beach is ;ove;y-- powdery sand, clear water. There is seaweed (it's an ocean, fool...) and it is cleaned up daily. There really isnt that much of it. NThere are adequate chase lounges at the beach and anough umbrellas for all. The pool was more of a hit with my teenage children but was also clean and well maintained. I spent a lot of time on the beach with a book, an umbrella, and lots of various ddrinks from the beachside bar (both alcohilic and not). Mixed drinks were not strong, but since you're not charged by the drink anbd are in the hot sun it doesn't matter. Minor warning. Many women do not wear tops.- this is a european resort.Oddly, there were no mosquitos. What a SHAME! A lot of the complaints on the site seem to be a matter of either bad luck or inflated expectatins (e.g. they change the sheets weekly-- well, I don't change them more often at home!) Also it is a tropical third world country with a Spanish influence. Don't expect ANYTHING to move fast!Oh, I do recommend leaving tips- the staff is probably not paid all that well, this is a poor county, and if you can afford almost $1,000 for a vacation per person, a few 100 peso bills (about $3.50) is no big deal. Dollars are, by the way accepted-- especiall on the 2 nights a week when local merchants sell jewelry and artworks. These folks are pushy salesmen, and you should vigorously bargain with them-- it's expected.I have been to a number of beautiful places (Kauai, Bermuda, Wyoming, Nova Scotia, PEI) and live in one (New Hampshire). This is one of the most stunning places I've seen and the most relaxing vacation ever.

<Author>hugsxo
<Content>Wonderful Vacation at Natura Park! Just returned from a visit to Natura Park Eco Resort and Spa Feb. 19 to 26 with Air Canada Vacations and had a wonderful holiday. We were very concerned about malaria, norovirus before leaving so decided to take the malaria medication Malaron - no side effects whatsoever - and was glad we did as there were some mosquitos. This resort is surrounded by water and mangroves and lots of other beautiful vegetation so we expected a few insects. On Wednesday evening fogging for mosquitos was done.The flights with Air Canada were on time with full meal and bar service and the transportation at Punta Cana airport well organized with large air conditioned buses, music and very friendly tour guide provided by the Dominican tourist service. Check-in at the hotel was very fast and the porter showed us promptly to our room, although one can carry one's own luggage without being hassled. We took an all-inclusive package but tipped on several occasions because the staff works very hard, long hours and appreciate their efforts being rewarded.The resort should be rated 5 stars for the surroundings, quality of service and cleanliness.Our room was near the main buffet, ground level with a small patio. Everything worked as it should from the hair dryer to the air conditioning to the minibar which was restocked every day. Warning! Only certain items in the fridge are free - these are mentioned at check in - other items, including the small bottles of water must be paid for. However, the maid regularly provided us with as many large bottles of water as we needed. We simply put the large bottle on top of the Pepsi in the fridge to chill. The water in the taps and shower has been chlorinated but should not be drunk. All water used for food preparation has been treated and it is perfectly safe to use ice cubes.Our room was spacious and spotlessly clean. We left a small tip each day for the maid together with a brief note on whatever extras we wanted - tissues, etc. - and the items were always provided. The coffeemaker was missing but was provided when we requested it. The air conditioning does stop when the door to the patio is opened. And the key tag has to be inserted into a slot for the electricity to work. When our maid noticed that we liked the air conditioning on, she simply stuck a comb (which was provided with the toilet articles) in the electricity slot and voila! our room was cool upon our return. Satellite television provided programming in English, German and Spanish so we kept up to date with CNN.The food was good with lots of variety. There was a selection of items for a custom-made omelet, choices of fruits for smoothies and a variety of hot and cold items for all meals. The food was served in smaller bowls and platters and the buffet was restocked regularly so there was no fear of anything spoiling. Wine was served generously with lunch and dinner. Thursday night is Dominican night at the buffet with a choice of national dishes in addition to regular menu items and the restaurant was beautifully decorated. Vendors arrive to sell there wares for those who don't want to walk to the beach shops which are just past the Allegro resort next door. And you are expected to barter with the hotel vendors as well.There are 3 a la carte restaurants - Italian (La Gondola, which is a portioned off section of the main buffet), seafood (La Perla at the beach) and steak (Media Luna on stilts over the pond with pink flamingos). We booked our alloted 3 visits the first day there very quickly with Guest Services. The food and service at those three locations are superb. A sip from your wine glass brings a server to promptly replenish. Even at the buffet as well as at the a la carte restaurants there are white table linens, napkins and fresh flowers. Don't miss out on the lobster at La Perla and the Tournedos at Media Luna. The salmon at La Gondola was perfectly cooked and lightly covered in a delicious caper butter sauce. And the desserts are to die for! Any chocoholic will be happy here!The beach was uncrowded and we found shady space at any time of the day. However, it had been and was quite windy for the first 3 days of our holiday so there was some seaweed in the water and the ocean bottom had been churned up. But men work every day cleaning the seaweed off the beach. There are the usual water sports and at the Allegro there are parasailing and banana boat rides for a fee. Typical Dominican weather returned by Wednesday - hot and humid with a wonderful breeze at the beach.There are international brand name liquors in addition to local brands. The bartenders work very hard and are always smiling whether given a tip or not. The staff give the appearance that they really enjoy their jobs. Try the espresso at the main bar.For those travelling with young children there is a mini club with attendant to watch the small ones. There is a wading pool as well as a beautiful free form pool and jaccuzi and a swim-up bar under a waterfall. The bar at the pool is open air for those who don't enjoy the cigarette smoke at the lobby bar or the show room bar.Entertainment on the nights we watched was excellent. The performers all have other jobs to do during the day but put on a spirited performance of dancing and singing in the evening. Hats off to them! There was a live band, a children's participation show and several animators to dance with the singletons.There is a very nice spa or one can have a massage at the beach. My husband used the gym 5 times while he was there and there was a supervisor at the facility. Weightlifting, step machines, and cycles are provided. At the beach instruction is proved in aerobics, water exercises, merengue lessons and various games. There is an archery target as well as beach volleyball.Beach towel service was excellent - usually you are allotted one towel for the day and if you turn it in, then you wait until the next day to exchange your card for a new one. But we were offered a clean towel upn exchange. At the towel house there are books, an assortment of games and the opportunity to book horseback riding. Several representatives wander the beach for go karting and visits to the Manatee Park. Tours can be booked with the vacation package representatives.This resort seems very popular with Spanish-speaking people, Germans, French, Italians, Russians, but not too many English-speaking people. Our purpose for this vacation was to read, lounge and rest so we didn't mind the lack of interaction with our fellow residents. As it was university break, there were several groups in the 19 to 25 year age, none were rowdy or overimbibed that we saw. Women do go topless at the beach, but most covered up when leaving thier sun tanning spot. And some young children enjoyed being in their birthday suits!If anyone were to become ill at this resort, it would have to be self-inflicted! The bathrooms were spotless. I have never been to a resort where the bathrooms at the beach had marble floors and sinks, fresh flowers and a regular attendant.You can walk for miles on this beach, although there has been some damage from last fall's Hurricane Jeanne and parts of the beach are now quite narrow with 2 to 3 feet gouges having been taken out of the shoreline. Any damage to the resort has long since been repaired and workers were busy restaining the wooden bridges and stairs. The game room and library were out of commission for this work to be done. The grounds of the resort are a series of walkways and bridges over water areas beside manicured lawns, trees, shrubs and flowers, with geese, ducks, flamingos and peacocks and fish in the ponds. Very beautiful and well-maintained!For those who might be interested, there is a Catholic mass at the Allegro resort, a 5-minute walk away, at 8 p.m. on Sunday evening. Since most of the congregation was English at the mass we attended, my husband volunteered to do the readings.Late check-out is very well organized at this resort. If you wish to keep your room beyond 12 noon, the charge is $25 per person and a sheet advising this is put in your room the day before check-out. However, we opted to pack up and leave our bags at the locked and supervised baggage room. We enjoyed a full day at the beach, retrieved the one bag in which we had organized our toiletries and clothes and made use of the shower room facilites off the lobby. Then we enjoyed a last pina colada, watching the sunset from the cool lobby area while waiting for our bus to the airport.There is a well-stocked gift shop at the resort, but beware! Prices are in U.S. dollars and I noticed a very small bottle of PeptoBismal for $8. So just take along whatever you might need in plentiful supply or be prepared to pay much more than you would at home for items.The only negative point about this resort is that the show room and main buffet are located at the entrance area of the resort, which may mean a long walk if you have an ocean-view room. Also, we found the ventilation in the main bar and show room quite poor and were bothered by the cigarette smoke. But then we are spoiled since we live in a smoke-free city.Overall, this resort in my estimation should be rated more than 4 star. We have stayed at the Barcelo chain and the Allegro before it was taken over by Occidental and the service at Natura Park, the beauty and cleanliness of the surroundings and the cheerfulness and helpfulness of the staff certainly put it in a 5-star category. I hope you will enjoy it as much as we did!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Horrible Experience on all Counts On December 11, 2004 we had the unfortunate luck to stay at Natura Park for less than 24 hours. This hotel was closed for approximately two months in the fall of 2004 for remodelling and reopened about two weeks before our stay. Its reopening was obviously premature.We were a party of four; three adults and a child. We were assigned two first-floor rooms. In one of the rooms the air conditioner did not function, the toilet did not flush completely and there was a severe leak from the bathroom above. We reported these faults and no one ever came to inspect them, never mind repair them. We repeatedly requested ice for the other room and regardless to whom we spoke to were told that it was the responsibility of someone else.A note is in order here. We are all native Spanish speakers and residents of the Dominican Republic, therefore we should not have had communication problems nor unreasonable expectations of hotel staff in the Dominican Republic. We can only imagine how much more frustrating the experiences would be for non Spanish speakers.The following day we had breakfast and lunch. The child in the party ate a ham salad plate (with mayonnaise). A few hours after lunch and on our return trip to Santo Domingo she began to complain of stomach pains and nausea. Soon after she experienced projectile vomiting and that evening continued with abdominal pain and severe diarrhea. The next day we took her to a pediatrician and after a battery of tests, she was diagnosed with salmonella, an intestinal disease associated with typhoid fever which produces symptoms within only a few hours and contracted through contaminated food and often times from mayonnaise that has not adequately refrigerated.There are other gross failures that we could report, but these should suffice. There are many excellent hotels in the Bavaro/Punta Cana area to choose from. We recommend that one stays away from Natura Park.

Do your self a favor and spend the extra $$$ to stay at a 5 or 6 star. We usually do and will not skimp again. As they say You get what you pay for. I would return to Punta Cana again but stay at another resort.

<Author>halcyonlondon
<Content>Beautiful and highly recommended Spent five days at the Natura Park in late May. The resort is absolutely gorgeous, clearly the best we saw in the Punta Cana area. This was especially surprising since it was one of the less expensive choices. The grounds are impeccable--tropical modern architecture with rooms set around a series of intimate court-gardens which are particulary impressive at night. It's an exceptionally well-manicured place, with lush landscaped grounds and tranquil lagoons, free-roaming flamingoes and exotic birds. The food was reasonable, although nothing special or terribly memorable. Caters to European tastes, lots of sliced meats and cheeses, decent breads, stewed meats, vegetable and potato salads, casseroles, and high-calorie desserts. Disappointed with the lack of simple Dominican criollo fare. Natura Park has a very international feel--primarily Spanish, Austrian, German, and French guests with perhaps 10% Americans/Canadians---a very nice clientele. The place has a relaxed, decidedly upscale, atmosphere. Natura Park's beach is exceptional when compared with the Melia Caribe, Allegro, and Suncape--its immediate neighborbors. Natura Park's overall atmosphere was more peaceful and exclusive rather than wild and loud. Contemplated the Melia Caribe prior to booking, which is also quite nice, though we found the Natura Park far better overall. I highly recommend the hotel and Punta Cana for four or five nights of peace and relaxation. Over five days, one may wish to contemplate an area closer to Santo Domingo for easier access to other attractions beyond the beach.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We will go back!! We spent a week at the Natura in early May with our two boys aged 11  13. It is only about 20 minutes on the coach from Punta Cana airport which is a big bonus if you have to cross the atlantic to get there!!The grounds are fabulous and superbly maintained with many species of birds living in the resort ponds such as herons flamingos and very well fed geese! Although there is a lot of water in the grounds the mosquitos were not any worse than other places we have stayed.It is quite obvious that this is one of the older hotels on the island and some of the furntiure could do with upgrading, however the whole place including our rooms was spotless. The beds were comfortable and I think the matressses and bed linen had been replaced quite recently.Mini bar alert!! Some things are included and some not so do pay attention at reception when you check in. The chamber maid re-stocks the free water. The staff are very friendly and helpful. We had a leak from the room above and it was fixed the same day. They even left us a job sheet to tell us what they had done!!The main restaurant was very good with lots of choices especially for vegetarians. Nothing was left hanging around on the buffet either becuase it was eaten or replaced with a fresh dish every so offten. We tried the Italian restaurant as the others are meat and fish which didnt appeal to one or other of us. This was also good. We were served the red wine that we drink at home so that was fine!! Called Liria - Spanish- try it!! Dont panic if it is chilled we drink like that here in the summer!!I have to agree with the others that dominican beef is probably best avoided!The beach is endless and they work hard to get rid of the seaweed which cannot be avoided on this coast. Lots of activities on the beach and around the pool. If you do nothing else then at least borrow a snorkel and mask from the diving center on the beach. The fish are amazing!People will try to sell you excursions, however if you say no they will be just as happy to stand and have a chat. We did a full day self drive jeep safari in convoy. Driving is quite an adventure in itself. Make sure you adopt the attitude that all other drivers are blind and have no brakes and you wil be fine! The morning session was great with several interesting stops. But the afternoon dragged with lots of driving through quite uninteresting areas which was a pity.We all went horseriding which was a lovely way to spend a couple of hours. Book it near the pool. they will pick you up from reception and take you to the stables. the horses know exactly where to go so just sit and pretend you know what you are doing!!!So alll in all it was good. We all enjoyed ourselves. If you want a flash new hotel try somewhere else but if you want value for money then I would give it a try.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>ABSOLUTELY THE BEST TIME!!! When I chose Natura Park, I was not sure what to expect. Most reviews I read were positive while others were not so positive. I decided that I would just need to see it for myself. I was wonderfully surprised by Natura Park. The grounds are well kept, and the natural surroundings are peaceful. The birds that live on the grounds are amusing, especially the duck family ( the little gosling was so precious). There are also flamingos, egrets, and some peacocks. There is so much natural diversity. For nature lovers, this place really delivers. (as a sidebar - I should also mention the mosquitos can be a bit uncomfortable. Bring bug spray.)The resort staff was very friendly. Many staff members can speak limited English, but I strongly recommend bringing along a spanish phrasebook. My attempts at Spanish really made the difference between being a stanger and being a friend. There is no disco at Natura Park, although, there is nightly entertainment that offers up variety shows, including karoke, and a mini disco. Not a big show by any means, but a fun time nevertheless. There is a little local spot down the beach - about a 10 minute walk. The place is small, but the dancing is fantastic. Staff members invited me to go, and we had the time of our lives. I went to Natura Park by myself, but I was not alone when I arrived. There are many Europeans, and of course, the locals. I met so many people from so many different places. I am glad that I brought my business cards. All in all, it was the absolutely best time I have ever had.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous! I had ready all of the reviews I could get my eyes on before we left, and I have to disagree with many, many of the complainers I read about. Yes, there was a bit of seaweed here and there and more on certain days, etc.; however, nothing overwhelming and certainly nothing to stop me from enjoying wading or swimming in the water. The buffet for breakfast and dinner did leave a bit to be desired, but I still managed to pack on some pounds, so there must have been enough to keep my hunger pangs from being outrageous - that and the constant food display down by the pool/beach throughout the day. When we first arrived, our room was not was we requested (not a King bed), but once we found out and told them that's not what we asked for, next thing we knew, we were in our King-bed room.We didn't understand a whole lot of the people around us as we were minority speaking English, and found that to be the perfect thing for relaxing. We knew enough spanish to make our way around, as well as found several other couples who too spoke English if we really felt we needed to rattle off a conversation with someone other than ourselves and the excellent bartenders who were always fun to try and communicate back and forth with (by the way - Jose down at the beach bar is the man you need to see - a little Mamma Wanna each night and you'll be set). The resort is perfectly located down from a shopping area, as well as it offers snorkeling, horse-back riding, parasailing, sun bathing, exercise, sports, and there are reps who offer taking a boat to other places to get dinner and/or do shopping elsewhere. I recommend the Lobster/seafood place (Langosta del Caribe) about 15 minutes down the beach by boat - fabulous food, more shops to see (inside a little community) and all the drinks you can take in while you sit and dine through a several-course, great meal. It even downpoured while we were eating, and the Cana tree awnings provided all the protection we needed - didn't get a drop on us! We brought the wash clothes as recommended in other reviews, but noticed there is one included in the hotel, it's just a little unnoticeable as it's in the basket under the shampoos, comb, etc. they provide for you... so if nobody ever seems to use it, yeah, I imagine people think the hotel doesn't have them. The room itself was cleaned very well, and the maid was excellent to us - leave a dollar next to the bottle of water and she'll bring you more bottles of water than you can even drink the next day.I highly recommend for buying your jewelry or pictures to take a walk down the beach to the left. There is a man that boats in his stuff daily and sells it cheaper than the gift shop and WITHOUT ANY HASSLE!Only thing I would have liked to see in Natura Park resort that wasn't offered is a disco place. I was hoping to dance a little while I was there, but that wasn't an option.I don't have any other experiences to compare it to as it's my first time being there, but I do know that I would return to Natura Park - great place, great people, great time, great sites. Wish I was there now!

<Author>pricecVt
<Content>A nice all inclusive My husband and I just returned from a week at the Natura Park Resort (April 17-24) and had a lovely time. We travel quite a bit to the Caribbean but this was my husband's first experience with an all-inclusive resort and he really enjoyed it.Rooms - as others have said, rooms are just okay. Nothing spectucalar but they were fine. True you do not get soap or wash clothes, so you should bring them along. Our room was on the back side of the resort in building IV on the second floor and it was extremely quiet. We were originally given a room in building XII but it was too close to the main restaurants/night club so we asked to switch. I think most of the rooms facing the courtyard were probably a bit noisier.The resort was at full capacity while we were there due to European holidays and US school vacation week so it was definltey busy and I think the staff did a great job with the number of people there. Most clientele was Euopean with the majority of people to be Spaniards, German, and French. Very few people from North America at our resort. It gave the resort a lovely international flavor which we really enjoyed.Beaches - beaches are lovely but listen to other's advice and get up and claim your lounge chair first thing in the morning, especially when the hotel is full. If you did not, there would be no lounge chair for you. This kind of surprised my husband but he was okay with it and we would get up at 7 am, go out to claim our chair and then go for a long walk along the beach to the left of the resort which was all Natural Park. We would be completely alone and then come back for a nice breakfast. Yes, the water has seawood but the works work tirelessly all day to keep the beaches clear for the guests. And one more word of advice for those that like to take long walks, bring your shoes along with you. When the sandy beach ends, you get to an area with a bit of coral and the beach walk becomes a hard sandy path next to the coral. The walk is beautiful and through a strand of palms that eventually leads to where the other resorts are. The walk is worth it but bare feet are definitely not comfortable there.The beach is also very, very busy so if you are looking for total solitude on the beach, then this is not the beach for you. Everyone is sunning, lounging, resting, etc. but the beach is extremely active. There are a myriad of boats in the water offering fishing trips, glass bottom boat tours, parasailing, jet boat rides, bumper boat rides, party boat tours, helicopter tours, etc. all in front of the 3 resorts on this beach. Additionally, every resort has all of their non-motorized water sports going on so there is always something happening. We like lots of quiet on the beach spending lots of time on Cape Hatteras in NC but this is a totally different experience so you have to be open minded and adjusted and enjoyed it.Beach bar was very fun and the beach lunch was enjoyable. They do have a drink list at both bars if you want to experiment with some of their more funky drinks. Try the mamajuana - which is a specialty rum drink they make at the resort - it is a combination of spices, rum, honey and I think red wine. It is a wild combination and very unique. But stay away from the grappa after dinner - it is like drinking lighter fluid!! We loved the beach bar for its breeze in the evening but spent more time at the front lobby bar which is classier and serves drinks with regular glasses. Bartenders are very friendly at both bars.Food - we loved the food. It was completely different at every meal and was not Americanized at all. Very European and Spanish flavor and we always found it interesting. My one complaint was that they didn't always tell you what each item was and you were guessing, but other than that we loved the food. We ate at Media Luna and La Perla restaurants. Both included wine with the meals and the wines were excellent as was the service at dinner.Shops were good in the resort and prices excellent. They did bring in local marketeers Thursday night if you want to bargain. There was also a little bargaining shack/village down the beach toward the sunscape. Lots of vendors in their own stalls. They are very aggressive but if you want to barter and get good deals this is the place to go. I personally found them to be a bit too aggressive for my tastes. They are very in your face.Hope you enjoy this resort if you choose to go.

<Content>Day Trips sold on the beach Our stay at Natura Park on the whole was a good one.We enjoyed the food and our hotel room was nice and clean. At check-in we were not told we needed to put a down-payment of $20.00 US or no remote control OR that we needed to ask to have someone unlock our fridge which made our first two hours in our room frustrating with returns and calls to the front desk. A few items of clothing went missing from our room. Some calls to their laundry for the articles, which just happened to be nice lingerie, went unanswered. People walk-in from the beach and use the bars, beach buffet and the night club and main buffet. I think this resort could use identification bracelets. One person to avoid on the beach is a young man named ORLANDO who sells short day-trips to a restaurant called Lagoustine for $40.00 US pp. He'll tell you you are going to see the Natura Pools and then go to the restaurant for lunch and that you get two free gifts you choose from Lagoustines gift shop. What happens is that you get dropped off at the restaurant a mile up the beach and you are given 2 for $1.00 items . No choice of gifts, no swim at the Natura Pools. The restaurant itself is a good beach restaurant but they should get rid of the guy putting $20.00 US grass hats on patrons heads while they're eating and the guy snapping your picture and trying to sell you a bottle of cheap rum with your picture on it for $15.00 US while you eat your dessert. The meal and boat ride there (we were told there would be 6 people in our boat and 14 showed up) weren't worth $80.00 US a couple. It's a gaff. Natura Park should simply get rid of this guy. There are other ways to get to see other areas including water taxis you can rent. The hotel beach was crowded but you can find a quiet spot up an endless beach. There are sand fleas so bring bug spray.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Smooth Operation! Just spent two good weeks here! Feb. 28th to March 14th, 2004. As you examine the brochures of this hotel you are led to believe that it is a secluded resort. This is not the case. The resort is one of three along this section of beach. Natura has the largest area of beach. The other two hotels are the Sunscape and an Allegro. Natura and Sunscape don't use identity wrist bands so you can move between the two easily!pNatura's beach is long and wide. There is plenty of white powder soft sand here. The busy section is in the centre. You can find a quieter spot alone on east end. There are plenty of chaises but you have to get up at 7 a.m. to use your towels to claim your spot. Then just go back to bed! If you want to see it, the sun rises at about 6:15 a.m. If you walk far enough to the west end of the beach you come to a rocky point. Walk up onto the grass and you will find a horseback trail, continue on west and you will come upon the Bavaro Hotels. It is about 5 kilometers all together. Wear plenty of sunscreen. The water is busy with water sports, parasailing, speed boats, helicopters, tour boats, party boats and scuba boats. There is a large reef about 2 kilometers out from the beach. The waves break on the reef thereby protecting the beach some what. There are 15 dive sites which are rotated to give you variety. They take place on the other side of the reef. There is shipwreck covered with beautiful coral, nurse sharks, sting rays and countless colouful fish. There is seaweed which washes onto the shore constantly. It is cleaned up daily. The beach water bottom is sandy.pThe hotel is kept very clean. The grounds are impeccable. There are a number of wooden bridges and large ponds filled with fish. 10 Healthy Flamigos, 8 Geese, 6 Egrets, a Heron, and a number of smaller species share the property. Rooms are spacious. The beds are firm and the shower water pressure and temperature is good. Bottled water is provided. The courtyards do echo a bit.pThe majority of the clientele is from Spain, France and Germany and some from North America. Kids are welcome here. You can book a baby sitter for $5.00US an hour. There are activities for them even a little dance time with a Clown in the evening. The entertainment is very professional. A cast of good dancers does their best to give you a fun show each night.pThere are some mosquitos. They fumigate the property every night at 7 p.m. A market is set up on Thursday nights. The quality of silver workmanship is poor The wood carvings are well done. The cigar vendor is selling counterfiet Cuban Cohibas in glass lidded boxes. Cohiba doesn't use this style of packaging.pInternational liquors! The food is good. Lots of fresh fruit juices and fruits like papaya, mango, pineapple and watermelon. Pasta bar, seafood. I found green beans, smoked salmon and Brie cheese! Stay away from the beef unless you like to eat leather. The a la carte restaurants were so so except that they served red Chilean wine which was very good. Did I forget anything? The beach bar is the most casual and is relaxed. They serve up a good lunch everyday. On saturday you get a great Paella cooked on a large beach barbecue.pWe arrived home rested and satisfied. We even made some new friends! Yes...I would go back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful, fun and relaxing We got back on the 9th of February and absolutely loved it. My wife and I went with our two friends, and we were accomodated with rooms directly across from each other that had views of the grounds (that looks like candy, they're so nice) and even a bit of the ocean. The little terraces each room has are very nice. Everything is pretty close, and the walk from the main buffet area to the rooms  then to the beach is extremely pleasant. I will try to hit a few thing other reviews may have missed.You can walk FOREVER...miles in either direction if you want to. We did that  it was extremely enjoyable. On the walk if you're thirsty, you can work out a deal with the kids to shimmy up the coconut trees and bring down  open cocos (10 pesos/20cents is a fair price per) that you can drink the milk of. On our long walks, we saw MANY other hotels (10, I'd say) and Natura Park was the nicest of all of them. The nicer walk is to the left, where you hit a very long stretch of undeveloped beach...but if you walk an hour or so, there are more hotels...pretty nice  you can use those restrooms and get drinks  food (though of course not for free).Speaking of food. I really liked it. There's always something pretty good  there's TONS of fresh juice (maybe 6 kinds) and fruit, including papaya, mango, pineapple, passion fruit, bananas, apples oranges etc. The variety is SIGNIFICANT...tons of stuff. This place is HUGE. I've never seen so many people eating in one place...and overall things are pretty efficient  well managed. It actually did rain a bit on 2 or 3 days, but cleared off  was sunny after an hour. This time of year gets very little rain...more in the summer  fall.We did an excursion, renting a car at the hotel (handy) for $70 a day  going to Santa Domingo. Long drive for one day. Car died, but we got immediate service  a new car in Santa Domingo, so had an easy trip. We came back to just vegetate on the beach, drinking the pina coladas  eating too much. Easy way to go. I would absolutely recommend it.Lets see, the gym is OK and there are lots of fun activities, dancing and games if you're into that kind of thing. Crowd was not rowdy at all  probably with a median age of 40 or so.Last issue is nationality, which has been discussed in other posts. We came with a Spanish group as my wife is Spanish  our friends are Spanish  Irish (I'm American). I would say about half American or Canadian and almost all the rest European, with good Spanish  German representation, some French, a few Russians, etc. We found it very very fun to watch people  gossip. Pina Coladas facilitate this sort of activity.Thumbs up!
